Buyu — Sales and Trade

Ruling on Alteration of Item Before Defect Discovered
States ruling and evidence for alteration before defect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a buyer alters a purchased item before discovering a defect, and explain the legal basis using the athar of Ali.

Core Idea
An inseparable alteration blocks return; the buyer may only claim compensation to avoid riba.

In sales transactions, disputes often arise when a buyer discovers a defect after having made changes to the item. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the principle that once an inseparable change occurs, returning the item would create a suspicion of riba. This lesson examines the ruling, its examples, and its evidence from the practice of Ali (ra).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the buyer's alteration of the item before discovering a defect. Ruling: buyer cannot return the item but can claim compensation (naqsan).
This is the core legal outcome.
2
Understand the types of alteration
The alteration must be inseparable (ziyadah muttahida), e.g., sewing, dyeing, mixing. These cannot be removed without damaging the item.
Separable changes (e.g., adding a removable strap) have a different ruling.
3
Analyze the evidence
The athar of Ali regarding a slave-girl: after intercourse, she cannot be returned; only compensation. This establishes the principle that any inseparable change blocks return.
This is a sunnah ahad evidence, but considered reliable in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Derive the underlying principle
Returning an altered item would give the seller extra value (riba-like), so it is prohibited. The only remedy is the price difference between sound and defective item.
Riba avoidance is a key theme in Hanafi sales law.
5
Apply to new cases
Recognize any inseparable change triggers this ruling. For example, installing a car stereo, engraving jewelry, or mixing ingredients.
Always determine if the change is reversible without loss of value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثوب وخاطه او صبغه او لت السويق بسمن ثم اطلع على عيب رجع بنقصانه وليس للبائع ان يأخذه بعينه کرے گا۔ اور بائع کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ بعینہ مبیع کو لے لے۔ ر یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ مشتری کے پاس جانے کے بعد مبیع میں ایسی زیادتی ہو گئی کہ میچ سے الگ نہیں ہو سکتی۔ اب اگر مبیع کو واپس کرتے ہیں تو زیادتی کے ساتھ واپس ہوتی ہے۔ اس صورت میں سود کا شائبہ ہیکہ بائع نے سود لیا۔ اس لئے یہی ایک صورت ہے کہ صحیح اور عیب دار مبیع میں جو فرق ہے وہ وصول کرے۔
(۱) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے عن عـلـى فـي رجل اشترى جارية فوطئها فوجد بها عيبا قال لزمته ويرد البائع ما بين الصحة والداء وان لم يكن وطنها ردها (الف) (سن لیتی ، باب ماجاء فیمن اشتری جاریۃ فاصا بھائم وجد بھائیاج خامس ص ۵۲۶، نمبر ۱۰۷۴۵ر مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الذى يشترى الامته فتقع علیهاج ثامن ص ۱۵۲ نمبر ۱۴۶۸۴) اس اثر میں باندی سے وطی کرنے کے بعد عیب کا پتہ چلا تو باندی کو واپس نہیں کر سکتا بلکہ نقصان واپس لینے کا حکم دیا۔ اس طرح کپڑا کاٹ کرسی لیا تو کپڑے میں زیادتی ہوگئی۔ یا رنگ دیا تو زیادتی ہو گئی یا ستو کو گھی میں ملالیا تو ستو میں ایسی زیادتی ہو گئی کہ الگ نہیں ہو سکتی۔ اس لئے نقصان کا رجوع کرے گا۔ اور بائع اس مبیع کو واپس لینا چاہے تو نہیں لے سکتا کیونکہ اس مبیع میں زیادتی ہو گئی۔ اب اگر اس کو واپس لیگا تو زیادتی ہونے کی وجہ سے ربوا اور سود کا شائبہ ہو گا۔ اس لئے اس مبیع کو واپس لینا چاہے تو نہیں لے سکتا۔
انوں مبیع میں زیادتی ہو جائے پھر عیب دیکھے تو رجوع بالنقصان کرے گا۔
The cloth, if he cuts it and sews it, or dyes it, or mixes sattu (barley flour) with ghee, then discovers a defect, he claims compensation for the defect, and it is not permissible for the seller to take it in kind. The buyer does that, and the seller is not allowed to take the item back. The principle is that after going to the buyer, such an increase (improvement) has occurred in the item that it cannot be separated. Now if the item is returned, it returns with the increase. In that case, there is a suspicion of usury (riba) because the seller would be taking something extra. Therefore, the only option is to receive the difference between the sound and defective item. (1) Evidence for this is the athar from Ali regarding a man who bought a slave-girl and had intercourse with her, then found a defect: he said, 'She becomes binding on him, and the seller returns the difference between soundness and defect; but if he had not had intercourse, he could return her.' (Sunan? and Mussanaf Abd al-Razzaq) In this athar, after intercourse, the slave-girl cannot be returned, only compensation for the defect is taken. Similarly, if the cloth is cut and sewn, an increase has occurred; or if dyed, an increase occurred; or if sattu is mixed with ghee, an inseparable increase occurred. So he claims compensation. The seller cannot take it back because an increase has occurred. If he takes it back, due to the increase, there is suspicion of riba. Therefore, he cannot take it back. If an increase occurs in the item, then he sees the defect, he claims compensation.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for a case where the buyer makes an inseparable alteration to the purchased item before discovering a defect. The examples given: cutting and sewing cloth, dyeing it, or mixing sattu (a type of grain) with ghee. In each case, a substantial change (ziyadah) has occurred that cannot be undone. The Hanafi ruling is that the buyer can only claim the compensation (the difference in value due to the defect) and cannot return the item, nor can the seller demand its return. The proof is the well-known athar from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) regarding a slave-girl: after intercourse (a change), she cannot be returned, only the difference is taken. The underlying principle is that returning the item with the extra improvement would lead to a suspicion of riba, as the seller would be getting something more than what he sold. This prevents any unfair gain. The commentary emphasizes that the seller cannot force the return because the increase is now part of the item.

Key Terms
الزيادة (al-ziyadah): An increase or improvement in the item that is inseparable, such as sewing, dyeing, or mixing.
الربوا (al-riba): Usury or unjustified increase. Here, the concern is that returning an item with an improvement would give the seller something extra, resembling riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer dyes a cloth after purchase and then discovers a defect, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The buyer can return the dyed cloth and get a full refund.
B) The buyer can claim compensation for the defect but cannot return the cloth.
C) The seller can demand the dyed cloth back.
D) The buyer must keep the cloth without any compensation.

Key Takeaway
An inseparable change to a purchased item blocks the right of return; the buyer's only remedy is compensation for the defect, to avoid riba.

Ruling on Defect After Manumission or Death of Slave
Explains the ruling and proof for claiming compensation after manumission or death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a slave is freed or dies before a defect is discovered and identify the proof from the athar of al-Zuhri.

Core Idea
After manumission or death, the buyer cannot return the slave but must claim compensation for the defect.

In sales, when a defect is discovered after the item is no longer in the buyer's possession due to manumission or death, the buyer's right to return the item is blocked. However, the seller's liability for hidden defects persists, and the buyer can claim the difference in value caused by the defect. This lesson explores the Hanafi position and its proof from the practice of the Salaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the preclusive events
The two events that block return are manumission (the buyer frees the slave) and death (the slave dies naturally). In both cases, the property in the slave is extinguished, making return impossible.
Note that if the buyer caused the death intentionally, the ruling may differ.
2
State the ruling that applies
The Hanafi ruling is that the buyer cannot return the slave but can claim compensation (naqsan) – the difference between the sound value and the defective value at the time of sale.
This is wajib on the seller.
3
Locate and analyze the proof
The proof is the athar of al-Zuhri: 'After death, deduct from him the amount of the defect.' This is a mursal hadith (zanni thubut) but accepted by the Hanafis as evidence.
The athar directly supports the ruling that compensation is due even after death.
4
Distinguish from the general rule of khiyar al-ayb
Normally, under khiyar al-ayb, the buyer can return the defective item. Here, because the item's ownership has been extinguished, return is blocked and only compensation remains.
This is a specific exception within the larger framework of defect liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۸۷۸](۸) ومن اشترى عبدا فاعتقه او مات عنده ثم اطلع على کرے گا۔
تشر غلام مر گیا اس کے بعد عیب کی اطلاع ہوئی تو غلام کو واپس نہیں کر سکتا لیکن مشتری کا حق بائع کے پاس رہ گیا جس کو واپس کرنا ہے تو یہی ہو سکتا ہے کہ نقصان کا رجوع کرے۔ یہ بھی نہیں ہے کہ مشتری نے جان کر مارا ہے کہ یہ کہہ سکے کہ مشتری اس عیب پر راضی تھا بلکہ یہ قدرتی طور پر مرا ہے اس لئے رجوع بالنقصان کرے گا ۔ اثر میں ہے عن الزهرى فى العهدة بعد الموت قال ينقص عنه بقدر العيب (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب العمدة بعد الموت والعتق ج ثامن ص ۶۳ نمبر ۱۴۷۲۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مرنے کے بعد عیب کی مقدار نقصان کا رجوع کرے گا ۔ اس طرح غلام آزاد کیا پھر عیب پر مطلع ہوا تو نقصان کا رجوع کرے گا۔ (۱) آزاد ہونا انسان کا انسانی حق ہے اس لئے مولی نے آزاد کیا تو اس کو اس کا انسانی حق دیا تو جو ہونا چاہئے وہی کیا تو آزاد کرنا غلام کے حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت علی سے مروی ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے باندی خریدی اور اس سے ولی کی ۔ پھر اس میں عیب پایا تو فرمایا کہ باندی مشتری کو لازم ہوگئی۔ اور بائع تندرست اور عیب کے درمیان جو فرق ہے وہ واپس کرے۔ اور اگر باندی سے وطی نہ کی ہوتی تو باندی واپس کر سکتا تھا (ب ) حضرت زہری سے غلام کی موت کے بعد عہدے کے بارے میں یہ ہے، فرمایا عیب کی مقدار اس سے کم کر دیا جائے گا۔
(8) And whoever buys a slave and then frees him, or he dies at his place, then he discovers a defect, he claims compensation. Explanation: The slave died, then after that he was informed of the defect, so he cannot return the slave, but the buyer's right remains with the seller which must be returned, so the only possibility is to claim compensation. It is not that the buyer intentionally killed him so that it could be said he was satisfied with the defect; rather, he died naturally, so he claims compensation. There is an athar from al-Zuhri concerning the warranty after death: he said, 'Deduct from him the amount of the defect.' (Mussanaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on warranty after death and manumission, vol. 8, p. 63, no. 14724) This athar states that after death, he claims compensation for the amount of the defect. Similarly, if he frees the slave and then discovers a defect, he claims compensation. (1) Emancipation is a human right, so when the master freed him, he gave him his human right, doing what was necessary. Commentary: (a) Narrated from Ali: A man bought a slave-girl and had intercourse with her, then found a defect: he said the slave-girl becomes binding on him, and the seller returns the difference between sound and defective; if he had not had intercourse, he could return her. (b) From al-Zuhri: Regarding the warranty after death, he said, 'The amount of the defect is deducted from it.'
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling when the buyer has either freed the slave (manumission) or the slave dies after purchase, and then a defect is discovered. In both cases, the item cannot be returned because the property has been extinguished (manumission transfers ownership to the slave) or the subject matter has perished. The Hanafi ruling is that the buyer can claim compensation (the difference in value due to the defect) from the seller. The proof is the athar of al-Zuhri, which explicitly states that after death, the buyer gets a deduction equal to the defect. The commentary distinguishes that the death is natural, not caused by the buyer, otherwise the buyer's right might be affected. The footnote includes the athar of Ali (already mentioned in the previous lesson) but reinforces the principle that after an irrevocable change, return is blocked.

Key Terms
العتق (al-itiq): Manumission; freeing a slave, which transfers ownership to the slave and ends the buyer's ownership.
العهدة (al-'uhdah): Warranty or guarantee period after sale during which the seller is liable for defects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer frees a slave and later discovers a pre-existing defect, what is the remedy?
A) The buyer can reclaim the slave and get a refund.
B) The buyer can only claim compensation for the defect.
C) The buyer has no remedy because he freed the slave.
D) The seller must take the slave back.

Key Takeaway
After the subject matter of sale is extinguished by manumission or death, the buyer's remedy is limited to claiming compensation for the defect.

Irreversible Additions and Defect: Ruling and Proof
States the ruling when buyer alters goods then discovers a defect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a buyer makes irreversible additions to defective goods and explain the proof from the Athar of Ali.

Core Idea
Irreversible additions bar return; only the price difference is claimable to prevent riba.

When a buyer modifies purchased goods in a way that cannot be undone, a defect discovered later cannot trigger a full return. This lesson explores the rule and its basis in the Athar of Ali (RA). You will learn the remedy of claiming the value difference and understand why the seller cannot take back the altered item.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what the buyer did (cut, dyed, mixed) and what the passage says: the buyer claims the deficiency (arash) and the seller cannot take the goods back.
The act is an irreversible addition (ziyadat muttasi'a).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the Athar of Ali (RA) about a slave-girl after intercourse.
The hadith is mursal but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the slave-girl case applies: intercourse is an irreversible addition, so the slave is not returned. Similarly, cutting cloth, dyeing, or mixing are irreversible; thus the goods are not returned.
The analogy is based on the common effective cause (illa) of irreversible addition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow return with compensation for the addition, but Hanafis prohibit return to avoid riba.
The difference stems from the Shafi'i view that return is allowed with compensation for the addition, while Hanafis see riba risk.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi position is mufta bihi: the prohibition of riba takes precedence, so return is blocked and only arash is claimed.
This is the established ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثاني ٣٨ كتاب البيوع الثوب وخاطه او صبغه او لت السويق بسمن ثم اطلع على عيب رجع بنقصانه وليس للبائع ان يأخذه بعينه [٨٧٨](٨) اور بائع کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ بعینہ مبیع کو لے لے۔ ر یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ مشتری کے پاس جانے کے بعد مبیع میں ایسی زیادتی ہو گئی کہ میچ سے الگ نہیں ہو سکتی۔ اب اگر مبیع کو واپس کرتے ہیں تو زیادتی کے ساتھ واپس ہوتی ہے۔ اس صورت میں سود کا شائبہ ہیکہ بائع نے سود لیا۔ اس لئے یہی ایک صورت ہے کہ صحیح اور عیب دار مبیع میں جو فرق ہے وہ وصول کرے۔ (١) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے عن عـلـى فـي رجل اشترى جارية فوطئها فوجد بها عيبا قال لزمته ويرد البائع ما بين الصحة والداء وان لم يكن وطنها ردها (الف) (سن لیتی ، باب ماجاء فیمن اشتری جاریۃ فاصا بھائم وجد بھائیاج خامس ص ٥٢٦، نمبر ١٠٧٤٥ر مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الذى يشترى الامته فتقع عليهاج ثامن ص ١٥٢ نمبر ١٤٦٨٤) اس اثر میں باندی سے وطی کرنے کے بعد عیب کا پتہ چلا تو باندی کو واپس نہیں کر سکتا بلکہ نقصان واپس لینے کا حکم دیا۔ اس طرح کپڑا کاٹ کرسی لیا تو کپڑے میں زیادتی ہوگئی۔ یا رنگ دیا تو زیادتی ہو گئی یا ستو کو گھی میں ملالیا تو ستو میں ایسی زیادتی ہو گئی کہ الگ نہیں ہو سکتی۔ اس لئے نقصان کا رجوع کرے گا۔ اور بائع اس مبیع کو واپس لینا چاہے تو نہیں لے سکتا کیونکہ اس مبیع میں زیادتی ہو گئی۔ اب اگر اس کو واپس لیگا تو زیادتی ہونے کی وجہ سے ربوا اور سود کا شائبہ ہو گا۔ اس لئے اس مبیع کو واپس لینا چاہے تو نہیں لے سکتا۔ انوں مبیع میں زیادتی ہو جائے پھر عیب دیکھے تو رجوع بالنقصان کرے گا۔
The book of sales: If a cloth is cut, or dyed, or sawiq is mixed with ghee, then a defect is discovered, he returns the deficiency, and the seller may not take it back as it is. Evidence: from Ali regarding a man who bought a slave-girl and had intercourse with her, then found a defect; he said: It is binding on him, and the seller returns the difference between the sound and defective value. If he had not had intercourse, he would return her.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage states the ruling when a buyer makes irreversible additions to purchased goods (cutting cloth, dyeing, mixing sawiq with ghee) and later discovers a defect. The buyer cannot return the goods because they now contain an addition inseparable from the original. If he returned them, the seller would receive the addition, which could be construed as riba (interest). Therefore, the buyer claims the difference in value between sound and defective goods. The proof is the athar from Ali on a slave-girl: after intercourse (an irreversible addition), the slave-girl is not returned; only the price difference is claimed. The same applies to the examples given.

Key Terms
رجع بنقصانه (raja'a bi naqsaanihi): The buyer claims the difference in value between the sound and defective goods from the seller.
زیادت (ziyadat): An addition to the sold item that is inseparable (e.g., cutting, dyeing, mixing).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a buyer cuts a cloth into a shirt and then discovers a defect, what is the correct remedy?
A) He may return the cut cloth to the seller.
B) He must keep the cloth and claim the price difference from the seller.
C) He may claim the full purchase price back.
D) He may take the cloth back to the seller and receive a full refund.

Key Takeaway
Irreversible additions by the buyer after purchase bar returning the defective goods; the buyer's only remedy is to claim the value deficiency (arash) to avoid riba.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Defect After Buyer Destroys the Item
Intra-Hanafi dispute on buyer's destruction and defect claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding a buyer's right to claim a deficiency after destroying the purchased item, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When the buyer destroys the item, Abu Hanifa bars the claim; the Sahibayn allow it — the latter is the relied-upon position.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in sales law: the buyer kills the slave he purchased, or eats the food he bought, and then discovers a defect. The question is whether the buyer can still claim compensation for the defect from the seller. The Hanafi school is divided: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the buyer forfeits this right, while his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), argue that the buyer retains the right to claim the deficiency caused by the defect. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and identifies the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Recognise that the scenario involves the buyer destroying the item (by killing a slave or eating food) before discovering a pre-existing defect. The core dispute is whether the buyer's destructive act nullifies his right to claim the price deficiency.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and inferred reasoning
According to Abu Hanifa, the buyer has no recourse (lam yarji' 'alayhi bi shay'). The reasoning may be that the buyer's act of destruction prevents the seller from taking the item back, implying acceptance of the item in its current state, or that the buyer caused the loss.
The matn does not explicitly state Abu Hanifa's dalil; it is inferred.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the buyer can claim the deficiency (yarji'u bi nuqsan al-'ayb) because the buyer was unaware of the defect at the time of destruction, so his act does not indicate consent. The commentary compares this to natural death of the item, where deficiency is claimable. An athar from al-Sha'bi is cited as support.
The athar: a buyer freed a slave then found a defect; compensation was awarded.
4
Identify the mufta bihi and the basis for tarjih
The later Hanafi preference is for the Sahibayn's view, as indicated by the commentary's analogy to natural death (where deficiency is claimable). Thus, in fatwa, the buyer can claim the deficiency.
The tarjih is made by the commentator, not by the matn itself.

Source Text

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثانى ٣٩ كتاب البيوع عيب رجع بنقصانه [٨٧٩](٩) فان قتل المشترى العبد او كان طعاما فاكله ثم اطلع على عيبه لم يرجع عليه بشيء في قول ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا يرجع بنقصان العيب خود بخود مرنے کی طرح ہو گیا اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی نقصان وصول کرے گا (٢) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے عن الشعبي ان رجلا ابتاع عبدا فاعتقه ووجد به عيبا فقال يرد على صاحبه فضل ما بينهما ويجعل ما رد عليه في رقاب لانه قد كان وجهه (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب العهدة بعد الموت والعتق ج ثا من ص ٦٤ نمبر ١٤٧٢٧) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ آزاد کرنے کے بعد عیب کا پتہ چلا تو نقصان وصول کرے گا۔ اصول خود بخود بیع ہلاک ہو جائے اور بعد میں عیب کا پتہ چلے تو چونکہ یہ شائبہ نہیں ہے کہ مشتری اس عیب سے راضی تھا اس لئے بائع سے نقصان وصول کرے گا۔
If the buyer kills the slave, or if it was food and he ate it, then discovers a defect: according to Abu Hanifa, he claims nothing; the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he claims the deficiency of the defect.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. When the buyer himself destroys the sold item (by killing a slave or eating food) and later discovers a defect, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the buyer cannot claim any deficiency because his own act of destruction indicates acceptance of the item as is, or because the buyer has prevented the seller from taking it back. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) argue that the buyer was unaware of the defect, so he still has the right to claim the deficiency, as he did not consent to the defect. The commentary compares this to death from natural causes, where deficiency is claimable. It also cites the athar from al-Sha'bi about a freed slave, which supports the Sahibayn's position. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is generally that of the Sahibayn in cases of destruction, as it is more in line with the principle of protecting the buyer from latent defects.

Key Terms
لم يرجع عليه بشيء (lam yarji' 'alayhi bi shay'): Buyer has no recourse against seller for any compensation.
يرجع بنقصان العيب (yarji'u bi nuqsan al-'ayb): Buyer claims the deficiency caused by the defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, if a buyer eats food and then discovers a defect, what is his right?
A) He has no claim because he consumed the food.
B) He can claim the full price of the food.
C) He can claim the deficiency caused by the defect.
D) He can return the food but must pay for what he ate.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a buyer who destroys the item before discovering a defect can still claim the price deficiency, following the Sahibayn's view.

Returning a Defective Item in a Chain Sale: The Qadi's Ruling Condition
States a condition for the first buyer's right to return to the original seller

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a first buyer may return a defective item to the original seller in a chain sale and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
A first buyer can only pass back a returned defect to the original seller if the sub-buyer's return was enforced by a qadi's ruling.

In a chain sale—A sells to B, B sells to C—what happens if C discovers a defect and returns the item to B? Can B then return it to A? This ruling clarifies that B's recourse against A depends on how B accepted the return from C. Only if a qadi (judge) ordered the return does B gain the right to pass it back uphill. This principle guards against unfair burden on original sellers when intermediate buyers voluntarily accept returns.

Guided Path
1
Identify the chain sale structure
Map the parties: original seller (A), first buyer (B), sub-buyer (C). The item (slave) travels from A to B to C.
2
Recognize the defect scenario
C discovers a pre-existing defect and returns the item to B. The ruling asks: can B now return it to A?
3
Recall the condition: qadi's ruling
B can only return to A if B accepted the return from C 'bi qada' al-qadi'—by the ruling of a judge. Voluntary acceptance does not create the same right.
A qadi's ruling makes the return legally binding, akin to an involuntary return.
4
Distinguish voluntary vs. judicial return
If B voluntarily accepted the return, it is treated as a new sale between B and C, not a cancellation of the original sale. Thus A is not obliged to take it back.
5
Apply to a new chain sale
Given a scenario where B voluntarily accepts a defective item from C, explain why B cannot return it to A. If the return was by court order, explain why B can.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٨٨٠] (١٠) ومن باع عبدا فباعه المشترى ثم رُدَّ عليه بعيب فان قبله بقضاء القاضي فله ان يرده خود بخود مرنے کی طرح ہو گیا اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی نقصان وصول کرے گا (٢) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے عن الشعبي ان رجلا ابتاع عبدا فاعتقه ووجد به عيبا فقال يرد على صاحبه فضل ما بينهما ويجعل ما رد عليه في رقاب لانه قد كان وجهه (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب العهدة بعد الموت والعتق ج ثا من ص ٦٤ نمبر ١٤٧٢٧) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ آزاد کرنے کے بعد عیب کا پتہ چلا تو نقصان وصول کرے گا۔ اصول خود بخود بیع ہلاک ہو جائے اور بعد میں عیب کا پتہ چلے تو چونکہ یہ شائبہ نہیں ہے کہ مشتری اس عیب سے راضی تھا اس لئے بائع سے نقصان وصول کرے گا۔
Whoever sells a slave and the buyer resells him, then he is returned to the first buyer due to a defect: if he accepts him by the qadi's ruling, he has the right to return him (to the original seller). If not accepted by qadi's ruling, he cannot return him.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This ruling addresses a chain sale: A sells to B, B sells to C. C returns the slave to B due to a defect. If B accepts the return by the ruling of a qadi (i.e., a court judgment), then B can in turn return the slave to A. This is because the qadi's ruling makes the return legally binding. If B accepted the return voluntarily without a qadi's ruling, the return is considered a new transaction between B and C, and B cannot then force A to accept the slave back. The commentary ends the section with a general principle: if the sold item is destroyed naturally and then a defect is discovered, the buyer can claim the deficiency because there is no suspicion that he accepted the defect. This wraps up the discussion of defects in sales.

Key Terms
بقضاء القاضي (bi qada' al-qadi): By the judgment of a qadi; a court order that makes the return binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a chain sale, if the sub-buyer returns a defective slave to the first buyer, what condition must be met for the first buyer to then return the slave to the original seller?
A) The sub-buyer must return the slave within a week.
B) The first buyer must have accepted the return by the ruling of a qadi.
C) The original seller must agree in writing.
D) The first buyer must pay the full price to the original seller first.

Key Takeaway
In a chain sale, the first buyer's right to return a defective item to the original seller hinges on whether the sub-buyer's return was accepted by a qadi's ruling—voluntary acceptance does not suffice.

Buyer's Recourse for Defect After Destroying the Item
Intra-Hanafi ruling on defect compensation after buyer destroys item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) on the buyer's right to seek deficiency compensation after destroying the item, and explain the basis for each view.

Core Idea
Destroying the item before discovering a defect does not automatically forfeit compensation: the buyer's ignorance preserves his right per Sahibayn.

When a buyer destroys or consumes the purchased item and only later discovers a defect, the Hanafi school is divided on whether he can still claim the deficiency in value from the seller. This lesson unpacks the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and the evidence each side presents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal question
The scenario: buyer kills a slave or eats food, then discovers a defect that existed at the time of sale. The question: can the buyer recover the difference in value between a sound and defective item?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa says no recourse. His reasoning: the buyer's act prevents return of the item, and the act may indicate satisfaction with the defect. The buyer assumed the risk by destroying.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani say the buyer recovers the deficiency. Reasoning: the buyer was ignorant of the defect; his right to compensation is attached to the seller; the act of destruction does not forfeit that right. They cite the athar of al-Sha'bi and Ali.
The athar involves freeing a slave, which is analogous to destruction.
4
Identify the key difference in principle
Abu Hanifa focuses on the buyer's act as overriding the claim; the Sahibayn focus on the buyer's ignorance preserving the right. This reflects different weight given to action vs. knowledge.
5
Note the mufta bihi and practical consequence
Later Hanafi practice often follows the Sahibayn. Practically, if the buyer destroys then discovers a defect, he can claim the deficiency if he was unaware; under Abu Hanifa he cannot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عيب رجع بنقصانه [۸۷۹](۹) فان قتل المشترى العبد او كان طعاما فاكله ثم اطلع على عيبه لم يرجع عليه بشيء في قول ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا يرجع بنقصان العيب خود بخود مرنے کی طرح ہو گیا اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی نقصان وصول کرے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے عن الشعبي ان رجلا ابتاع عبدا فاعتقه ووجد به عيبا فقال يرد على صاحبه فضل ما بينهما ويجعل ما رد عليه في رقاب لانه قد كان وجهه (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب العهدة بعد الموت والعتق ج ثا من ص ۶۴ نمبر ۱۴۷۲۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ آزاد کرنے کے بعد عیب کا پتہ چلا تو نقصان وصول کرے گا۔ اصول خود بخود بیع ہلاک ہو جائے اور بعد میں عیب کا پتہ چلے تو چونکہ یہ شائبہ نہیں ہے کہ مشتری اس عیب سے راضی تھا اس لئے بائع سے نقصان وصول کرے گا۔ (۸۷۹) (۹) پس اگر مشتری نے غلام کو قتل کر دیا یا کھانا تھا تو اس کو کھا لیا پھر اس کے عیب پر مطلع ہوا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول میں بائع پر کچھ بھی رجوع نہیں کرے گا۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا نقصان وصول کرے گا۔ مشتری نے غلام کو قتل کر دیا، یا بیج کھانا تھی اس کو کھا لیا پھر پتہ چلا کہ اس میں عیب ہے تو امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بائع سے نقصان وصول نہیں کرے گا۔ کیونکہ جب خود قتل کر دیا اور کھا لیا تو اب اگر بائع اس مبیع کو واپس مانگے تو مشتری نہیں دے سکے گا۔ اور یہ مشتری کے کرتوت سے ہوا تو گویا کہ مشتری کا عمل نے بھیج کو واپس نہیں ہونے دیا۔ اس لئے مشتری کو نقصان لینے کا حق نہیں ہو گا (۲) قتل کرنا اس بات پر دلیل ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ اس عیب سے راضی تھا۔ اس لئے بھی نقصان نہیں لے سکتا۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ نقصان لے گا۔ کیونکہ مشتری کو کیا پتہ کہ مبیع میں عیب تھا اس لئے وہ عیب سے راضی نہیں تھا۔ اور مشتری کا حق عیب بائع کے یہاں محبوس ہے۔ اس لئے وہ عیب کا نقصان بائع سے لے گا (۲) صاحبین کی دلیل او پر حضرت علی کا اثر ہے کہ عیب کا نقصان لے۔ یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ مشتری نے خود بیع کو ہلاک کیا ہو پھر عیب دیکھے تو نقصان لیگا یا نہیں۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نہیں لے گا، صاحبین کے نزدیک لے گا۔
Defect recourse by deficiency [879](9) If the buyer kills the slave, or if it was food and he ate it, then he discovers a defect, he has no recourse against the seller in the opinion of Abu Hanifa, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he recovers the deficiency of the defect. Similar to when it perishes on its own, so in this case also he will recover the deficiency. There is evidence for this in the athar from al-Sha'bi: A man bought a slave and freed him, then found a defect in him, so he said: He returns to his seller the difference between them, and whatever is returned is placed on his neck because he was the cause. From this athar it is understood that after freeing, if a defect is found, he will recover the deficiency. Principle: If the sale item perishes on its own and then a defect is discovered, since there is no suspicion that the buyer was content with the defect, he will recover the deficiency from the seller. (879)(9) So if the buyer killed the slave, or it was food and he ate it, then he becomes aware of its defect, according to Abu Hanifa he will not recover anything from the seller, but the Sahibayn say he will recover the deficiency. If the buyer killed the slave, or the seed was food and he ate it, then it became known that it had a defect, Abu Hanifa says he will not recover the deficiency from the seller, because when he himself killed and ate, now if the seller demands the item back, the buyer cannot return it, and this happened by the buyer's action, so it is as if the buyer's action prevented the item from being returned. Therefore the buyer has no right to take the deficiency. Also, killing can be evidence that he was content with the defect, so also he cannot take the deficiency. The Sahibayn say he will take the deficiency, because the buyer did not know the item had a defect, so he was not content with the defect. And the buyer's right due to the defect is held with the seller, so he will take the deficiency from the seller. The Sahibayn's proof is the athar of Ali that he took the deficiency of the defect. This issue is based on the principle: if the buyer himself destroys the sale item and then sees a defect, will he take the deficiency or not? According to Abu Hanifa, he will not take it; according to the Sahibayn, he will take it.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the buyer's right to seek compensation for a defect after the item has been destroyed or consumed by the buyer. The ruling is from Imam Muhammad's Zahir al-Riwayah. Abu Hanifa holds that the buyer loses all recourse because his own act (killing, eating) prevents return of the item, making it analogous to a situation where the buyer's action indicates satisfaction with the defect. The Sahibayn argue that the buyer was unaware of the defect at the time of destruction, so his right to compensation remains. They support their view with an athar from al-Sha'bi regarding a freed slave and an athar from Ali. The text also states a general principle: if the item perishes on its own, the buyer's right to deficiency remains. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position follows the Sahibayn in many later fatwa collections.

Key Terms
عيب (ayb): A defect in the sold item that existed at the time of sale and diminishes its value.
رجوع بنقصان (ruju' bi-nuqsan): The buyer's right to recover the difference in value between a sound and defective item from the seller.
صاحبين (sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two chief disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why does the buyer retain the right to claim deficiency after destroying the item?
A) Because the seller is always liable for defects
B) Because the buyer was ignorant of the defect at the time of destruction
C) Because destroying the item is a sign of satisfaction
D) Because the athar of Ali only applies to freeing, not killing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the buyer's destruction of the item does not automatically forfeit his right to claim deficiency if he was unaware of the defect at the time.

Resale and Return: The Effect of Qada' al-Qadi on the Buyer's Right to Return
Ruling on chain sales and return due to defect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a buyer who resold a defective item and then received it back by qadi's judgment can return it to the original seller, and distinguish it from voluntary acceptance without a qadi's judgment.

Core Idea
A buyer's resale forfeits return to original seller unless a qadi's judgment annuls the resale retroactively.

In chain sales, the first buyer may resell an item only to have it returned due to a defect. Can he then pass it back to the original seller? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer depending on whether the second return was enforced by a qadi's judgment. This lesson unpacks that key distinction and the underlying principle of impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Identify the chain: original seller (S) sells to buyer (B1). B1 resells to B2. B2 returns the item to B1 due to a pre-existing defect. The question is whether B1 can return it to S.
2
Identify the key condition: qadi's judgment vs voluntary
The ruling states that if B2's return was by qadi's judgment, B1 can return to S; if B2 returned voluntarily (without qadi), B1 cannot.
A qadi's judgment retroactively annuls the B1-B2 sale.
3
Apply the principle of impossibility
A buyer who does an act that makes return impossible (like resale) loses the right to return. A qadi's judgment negates that act, restoring the right.
Without the judgment, the resale remains a valid impediment.
4
Consider additional nuance: selling after discovering the defect
If B1 sold after discovering the defect, that indicates acceptance and forfeits return regardless of qadi's judgment. This is supported by an athar from Amir.
The athar: offering for sale after seeing defect implies consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۸۸۰] (١٠) ومن باع عبدا فباعه المشترى ثم رُدَّ عليه بعيب فان قبله بقضاء القاضي فله ان يرده على بائعه الاول وان قبله بغير قضاء القاضى فليس له ان يرده على بائعه الاول [۸۸۰] (۱۰) کسی نے غلام بیچا۔ پھر اس غلام کو مشتری نے دوسرے کے پاس بیچ دیا۔ پھر عیب کے ماتحت غلام مشتری پر واپس کر دیا گیا۔ پس اگر مشتری نے اس غلام کو قاضی کے فیصلہ سے قبول کیا تو اس کو حق ہے کہ اس غلام کو بائع اول کو واپس کر دے۔ اور اگر اس کو قاضی کے فیصلہ کے بغیر قبول کیا تو مشتری کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اس کو بائع اول پر واپس کرے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت شعمی سے منقول ہے کہ کسی آدمی نے غلام خریدا پھر اس کو آزاد کر دیا۔ بعد میں اس میں عیب پایا۔ فرمایا بائع پر دونوں کے درمیان فرق لوٹایا جائے گا ( یعنی صحیح اور عیب دار کے درمیان قیمت کا جو فرق ہو وہ بائع سے لیا جائے گا) پھر جو کچھ لوٹا یا وہ غلام کی گردن پر ڈالا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ وہی اس کا سبب بنا۔ الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثانى) كتاب البيوع عـلـى بـائـعـه الاول وان قبله بغير قضاء القاضى فليس له ان يرده على بائعه الاول [ ۸۸۱] (۱۱) ومن اشترى عبدا و شرط البائع البراءة من كل عيب فليس له ان يرده بعيب وان مثلا زید مشتری نے غلام خریدا، پھر اس کو دوسرے کے پاس بیچا، پھر مشتری ثانی خالد نے اسی عیب کے ماتحت جو پہلے بائع کے پاس تھا مشتری اول زید کو واپس کر دیا، تو زید بائع اول رحیم کے پاس واپس کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں؟ اس میں تفصیل یہ ہے کہ زید نے عیب کا انکار کیا پھر قاضی نے عیب کے ماتحت غلام کو واپس کرنے کا فیصلہ دیا جس سے مجبور ہو کر زید نے غلام کو قبول کیا تو اس صورت میں زید کو حق ہے کہ اس عیب کی وجہ سے غلام کو بائع اول رحیم کی طرف واپس کر دے۔ قاضی نے جب غلام واپس کرنے کا فیصلہ دیا تو زید اور خالد کے درمیان کی بیچ بالکل ختم ہو گئی گویا کہ کوئی بیع ہوئی ہی نہیں۔ اور مشتری نے گویا کہ کوئی ایسا کام نہیں کیا جس کی وجہ سے مبیع بائع اول رحیم کی طرف لوٹانا متعذر ہو ۔ قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ مشتری کوئی ایسا کام کرے جس سے بیع بائع کی طرف لوٹانا متعذر ہو جائے تو پھر مشتری عیب کی وجہ سے بائع کی طرف نہیں لوٹا سکتا۔ یہاں تو قاضی کے فیصلہ کی وجہ سے دوسری بیع نسیا منسیا ہوگئی۔ اس لئے مشتری نے گویا کہ کوئی ایسا کام کیا ہی نہیں جس کی وجہ سے طبیع کا واپس ہونا متعذر ہو۔ اس لئے مشتری زید بائع اول رحیم کی طرف مبیع واپس کر دے گا۔ اور قاضی کے فیصلہ کے بغیر مشتری زید نے خالد سے مبیع واپس لے لی تو زید اور خالد کی درمیان کی بیچ بالکل ختم نہیں ہوئی۔ اس کے اثرات باقی ہیں۔ اور وہ یہ ہے کہ زید کے بیچنے کی وجہ سے مبیع کو بائع اول رحیم کی طرف واپس کرنا متعذر ہو گیا۔ اور قاعدہ گزر گیا کہ کہ مشتری کے عمل سے مبیع کو بائع کی طرف واپس کرنا متعذر ہو جائے تو مشتری بیع کو بائع کی طرف واپس نہیں کر سکتا۔ اور اس صورت میں یہی ہوا کہ مشتری زید کے بیچنے کی وجہ سے مبیع کو بائع اول رحیم کی طرف واپس کرنا متعذر ہو گیا۔ اور قاضی کا فیصلہ بھی نہیں ہے کہ بیع نسیا منسیا ہو جائے۔ اس لئے زید مبیع کو بائع اول رحیم کی طرف واپس نہیں کر سکتا اگر عیب دیکھنے کے بعد بیچا ہو تو مبیع واپس نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ عیب دیکھنے کے بعد بیچنا اس بات پر دلیل ہے کہ وہ اس عیب پر راضی ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن عامر في الرجل يشترى السلعة فيرى بها العيب ثم يعرضها على البيع ليس له ان يردها (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی هیت ۷ ۵ فی الرجل یشتری السلعة فیجد بھا عیباج خاص ص ۱۱ نمبر ۲۳۲۳۱) اس اثر میں ہے کہ عیب دیکھنے کے بعد سامان کو بیچنے کے لئے پیش کیا تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ اس عیب سے راضی ہے۔ اس لئے اب اس کو بائع کی طرف واپس نہیں کر سکتا۔ اصول اگر مشتری کے عمل سے مبیع کو واپس کرنا متعذر ہو گیا تو مبیع کو بائع کی طرف واپس نہیں کر سکتا۔۔ [AN]
[880] (10) Whoever sells a slave, and the buyer sells him, then he is returned to him due to a defect: if he accepted him by the judgment of the qadi, he may return him to his first seller; if he accepted him without the judgment of the qadi, he may not return him to his first seller. [880] (10) Someone sold a slave, then the buyer sold him to another, then the slave was returned to the buyer due to a defect. So if the buyer accepted the slave by the qadi's decision, he has the right to return that slave to the first seller. If he accepted it without the qadi's decision, it is not permissible for the buyer to return it to the first seller. Footnote (a): It is narrated from Shami that a man bought a slave and freed him, then found a defect in him. He said: The difference between them is returned to the seller, and whatever is returned is placed on the slave's neck because he was the cause. (Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, vol. 2, Book of Sales) ... on his first seller, and if he accepted without the qadi's judgment, he may not return it to his first seller. [881] (11) Whoever buys a slave and the seller stipulates immunity from every defect, he may not return him due to any defect. And for example, Zayd the buyer bought a slave, then sold him to another, then the second buyer Khalid returned the slave to the first buyer Zayd due to the same defect that existed with the first seller. Then Zayd is able to return him to the first seller Rahim or not? The detail is: Zayd denied the defect, then the qadi gave a decision to return the slave due to the defect, compelling Zayd to accept the slave; in this case, Zayd has the right to return the slave to the first seller Rahim because of this defect. When the qadi gave the decision to return, the sale between Zayd and Khalid became completely void, as if no sale had occurred, and the buyer did not do anything that would make it impossible to return the item to the first seller. The rule is: if the buyer does something that makes it impossible to return the sale item to the seller, then he cannot return it to the seller due to the defect. Here, because of the qadi's decision, the second sale was annulled, so the buyer did not do anything that would prevent return. Therefore, the buyer Zayd will return the item to the first seller Rahim. And if without the qadi's decision, Zayd took back the item from Khalid, then the sale between Zayd and Khalid is not completely void; its effects remain. And that is that because Zayd sold it, it becomes impossible to return the item to the first seller Rahim. And the rule passed that if the buyer's action makes it impossible to return the item to the seller, then the buyer cannot return the sale to the seller. And in this case, it happened that because of Zayd's selling, returning the item to the first seller became impossible, and there is no qadi's decision to annul the sale. Therefore, Zayd cannot return the item to the first seller. If he sold it after seeing the defect, he cannot return it, because selling after seeing the defect is evidence that he is content with the defect. The proof is the athar from Amir: 'If a man buys a commodity and sees a defect in it, then offers it for sale, he has no right to return it.' This athar indicates that after seeing the defect, presenting it for sale means he is content with the defect, so he cannot return it to the seller. Principle: If the buyer's action makes it impossible to return the item, then he cannot return the item to the seller.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on a cascading sale scenario: the first buyer (Zayd) resells the slave to Khalid, who later returns it to Zayd due to a pre-existing defect. The question is whether Zayd can then return the slave to the original seller (Rahim). The text distinguishes two cases: (1) If the return from Khalid was enforced by a qadi's judgment, Zayd can return it to the original seller because the qadi's judgment effectively annuls the second sale ab initio, so Zayd's act of selling is treated as if it never happened, making return possible. (2) If Zayd accepted the return voluntarily without a qadi's judgment, the second sale remains valid in its effects, and Zayd's act of selling is an independent action that prevents return. The passage also notes an additional nuance: if Zayd sold after discovering the defect, it indicates acceptance, so he cannot return it. An athar from Amir is cited to support this. The underlying principle is that the buyer's action that makes return impossible forfeits his right to return. This is a ruling_statement with analogy and athar as proofs. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
قضاء القاضي (qada' al-qadi): A binding judgment issued by a qadi (judge) that resolves the dispute and renders the return as legally effective.
متعذر (muta'adhdhir): Impossible or prevented; used to describe when the item cannot be returned due to the buyer's action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi law, if a buyer resells an item and the second buyer returns it due to a defect voluntarily, can the first buyer return it to the original seller?
A) Yes, if the original seller agrees.
B) No, because the first buyer's resale makes return impossible.
C) Yes, because the defect existed at the original sale.
D) No, only if the second buyer used qadi's judgment.

Key Takeaway
A buyer's right to return a defective item to the original seller is preserved only if the second return was by qadi's judgment; otherwise, his own resale prevents return.

Seller's Condition of Immunity from All Defects
Ruling on the effect of a seller's stipulation of immunity from all defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the effect of a seller's stipulation of immunity from all defects and explain why the buyer cannot return the item.

Core Idea
A seller's explicit stipulation of immunity from all defects bars the buyer from returning the item for any defect, known or unknown.

In sales transactions, sellers sometimes include a condition exempting themselves from liability for defects. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on such a stipulation: when the seller explicitly states he is not responsible for any defect, the buyer loses the right to return the item, even for hidden defects. The ruling is based on the principle that the buyer accepted the risk.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The buyer cannot return the sold item due to any defect if the seller stipulated immunity from all defects.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the defects were named.
2
Understand the condition
The seller must explicitly stipulate 'immunity from every defect' or similar clear words.
A general disclaimer is sufficient; no enumeration needed.
3
Note the scope
The condition covers all defects, including hidden ones unknown at the time of sale.
The buyer is deemed to have accepted the item with all defects.
4
Recognize the rationale
The sale is concluded with that condition; therefore the buyer assumed the risk and forfeited the right of return.
This is based on the principle that contracts are to be honored as agreed.
5
Apply the principle
If the buyer later sells the item after discovering a defect, that action indicates acceptance and also bars return to the original seller.
As per the athar cited in the footnote.

[881] (11) Whoever buys a slave and the seller stipulates immunity from every defect, he may not return him due to any defect. And for example, Zayd the buyer bought a slave, then sold him to another, then the second buyer Khalid returned the slave to the first buyer Zayd due to the same defect that existed with the first seller. Then Zayd is able to return him to the first seller Rahim or not? The detail is: Zayd denied the defect, then the qadi gave a decision to return the slave due to the defect, compelling Zayd to accept the slave; in this case, Zayd has the right to return the slave to the first seller Rahim because of this defect. ... (repetition from earlier) ... Principle: If the buyer's action makes it impossible to return the item, then he cannot return the item to the seller. (AN) (11) Someone bought a slave and the seller stipulated immunity from every defect, so it is not permissible for the buyer to return him due to a defect, even if all defects were not named or enumerated. The seller said: 'Look and buy; I am immune from all defects and will not accept a return.' So even if every defect... Footnote (a): The athar from Amir: A man bought a commodity, saw a defect in it, then offered it for sale; he has no right to return it.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on a seller's stipulation of immunity (bara'ah) from all defects. According to the Hanafi school, if the seller explicitly states that he is not liable for any defects, the buyer forfeits the right to return the item for any defect, even if the defects were not specified. This is because the buyer accepted the sale with full knowledge of the disclaimer. The commentary then repeats the earlier detailed example about a cascading sale and returns, which seems to be a copyist's repetition. The original ruling (11) is concise and clear. The footnote cites the athar from Amir to support the principle that selling after seeing a defect indicates acceptance. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah. The passage is a ruling_statement with no explicit proof in the immediate text, but the footnote provides an athar.

Key Terms
البراءة من كل عيب (al-bara'ah min kull 'ayb): A stipulation by the seller that he is exempt from liability for any defect in the sold item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a seller stipulates 'I am immune from all defects,' can the buyer return the item for a hidden defect?
A) Yes, because the defect was hidden
B) No, because the stipulation covers all defects
C) Yes, if the defect is major
D) No, but only if the defect was known to the seller

Key Takeaway
A seller's explicit stipulation of immunity from all defects bars the buyer from returning the item for any defect, known or unknown, because the buyer accepted the sale on that condition.

Return of Defective Item After Resale and Court Judgment
Explains when a buyer can return defective item to original seller after reselling it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a buyer loses the right to return a defective item if his own action (e.g., resale) makes return impossible, unless a court judgment annuls the second sale retroactively.

Core Idea
A buyer's resale blocks return of a defective item unless a court annuls the sale.

This passage from a later Hanafi commentary explains a nuanced ruling from the fiqh of sales (buyu'). The issue is when a buyer discovers a defect in an item he purchased and then resold it. Can he still return it to his original seller? The answer depends on whether the second sale was undone by a court judgment or by mutual consent, and whether the buyer saw the defect before reselling. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the principle of impediment (ta'azzur) caused by the buyer's own action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is the first buyer returning a defective item to the original seller after having resold it. The ruling is that it is permissible if the return from the second buyer was via a court judgment, but not if done voluntarily.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar from 'Amir as proof that selling after seeing the defect indicates acceptance and forfeits the right to return.
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
3
Understand the underlying principle (qā'ida)
If the buyer's action makes return impossible, he loses the right to return. The court judgment removes the impediment by nullifying the second sale retroactively, as if the buyer never sold it.
The principle is derived from the commentary's reasoning.
4
Note the practical distinction (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference between a court-ordered return and a voluntary return determines whether the first buyer can pass the defect back to the original seller.
This is a key point for fatwa.

Source Text

سے غلام کو بائع اول رحیم کی طرف واپس کر دے۔ قاضی نے جب غلام واپس کرنے کا فیصلہ دیا تو زید اور خالد کے درمیان کی بیچ بالکل ختم ہو گئی گویا کہ کوئی بیع ہوئی ہی نہیں۔ اور مشتری نے گویا کہ کوئی ایسا کام نہیں کیا جس کی وجہ سے مبیع بائع اول رحیم کی طرف لوٹانا متعذر ہو ۔ قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ مشتری کوئی ایسا کام کرے جس سے بیع بائع کی طرف لوٹانا متعذر ہو جائے تو پھر مشتری عیب کی وجہ سے بائع کی طرف نہیں لوٹا سکتا۔ یہاں تو قاضی کے فیصلہ کی وجہ سے دوسری بیع نسیا منسیا ہوگئی۔ اس لئے مشتری نے گویا کہ کوئی ایسا کام کیا ہی نہیں جس کی وجہ سے طبیع کا واپس ہونا متعذر ہو۔ اس لئے مشتری زید بائع اول رحیم کی طرف مبیع واپس کر دے گا۔ اور قاضی کے فیصلہ کے بغیر مشتری زید نے خالد سے مبیع واپس لے لی تو زید اور خالد کی درمیان کی بیچ بالکل ختم نہیں ہوئی۔ اس کے اثرات باقی ہیں۔ اور وہ یہ ہے کہ زید کے بیچنے کی وجہ سے مبیع کو بائع اول رحیم کی طرف واپس کرنا متعذر ہو گیا۔ اور قاعدہ گزر گیا کہ کہ مشتری کے عمل سے مبیع کو بائع کی طرف واپس کرنا متعذر ہو جائے تو مشتری بیع کو بائع کی طرف واپس نہیں کر سکتا۔ اور اس صورت میں یہی ہوا کہ مشتری زید کے بیچنے کی وجہ سے مبیع کو بائع اول رحیم کی طرف واپس کرنا متعذر ہو گیا۔ اور قاضی کا فیصلہ بھی نہیں ہے کہ بیع نسیا منسیا ہو جائے۔ اس لئے زید مبیع کو بائع اول رحیم کی طرف واپس نہیں کر سکتا اگر عیب دیکھنے کے بعد بیچا ہو تو مبیع واپس نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ عیب دیکھنے کے بعد بیچنا اس بات پر دلیل ہے کہ وہ اس عیب پر راضی ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن عامر في الرجل يشترى السلعة فيرى بها العيب ثم يعرضها على البيع ليس له ان يردها (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی هیت ۷ ۵ فی الرجل یشتری السلعة فیجد بھا عیباج خاص ص ۱۱ نمبر ۲۳۲۳۱) اس اثر میں ہے کہ عیب دیکھنے کے بعد سامان کو بیچنے کے لئے پیش کیا تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ اس عیب سے راضی ہے۔ اس لئے اب اس کو بائع کی طرف واپس نہیں کر سکتا۔ اصول اگر مشتری کے عمل سے مبیع کو واپس کرنا متعذر ہو گیا تو مبیع کو بائع کی طرف واپس نہیں کر سکتا۔
For example, Zayd, the first buyer, bought a slave, then sold it to another person. Then the second buyer, Khalid, returned the slave to the first buyer Zayd due to the same defect that was present with the original seller. Can Zayd return it to the original seller, Rahim? The detail is: if Zayd denied the defect, then the judge ruled to return the slave due to the defect, and Zayd accepted the slave under compulsion, then in that case Zayd has the right to return the slave to the original seller Rahim because of that defect. When the judge ruled to return the slave, the sale between Zayd and Khalid was completely annulled, as if no sale had occurred. And the buyer did not do anything that would make it impossible to return the sold item to the original seller Rahim. The principle is: if the buyer does something that makes it impossible to return the item to the seller, then the buyer cannot return it to the seller due to the defect. Here, due to the judge's ruling, the second sale was annulled. Therefore, the buyer did not do anything that would make the return impossible. Thus, the buyer Zayd will return the sold item to the original seller Rahim. And if without the judge's ruling, the buyer Zayd took back the sold item from Khalid, then the sale between Zayd and Khalid is not completely annulled; its effects remain. That is, because of Zayd's sale, returning the item to the original seller Rahim has become impossible. And the principle has passed: if the buyer's action makes it impossible to return the item to the seller, then the buyer cannot return it to the seller. In this case, because of Zayd's sale, returning the item to the original seller Rahim became impossible. And there is no judge's ruling to annul the sale. Therefore, Zayd cannot return the sold item to the original seller Rahim. If he sold after seeing the defect, he cannot return the item, because selling after seeing the defect is evidence that he is satisfied with the defect. The evidence for this is the athar from 'Amir concerning a man who buys a commodity, then sees a defect in it, then presents it for sale: he has no right to return it. In this athar, when he presents the item for sale after seeing the defect, it means he is satisfied with the defect. Therefore, he cannot return it to the seller. The principle: if the buyer's action makes it impossible to return the sold item, then he cannot return the item to the seller.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling about the return of a defective item after the buyer has resold it. The commentator expands on the rule from the matn, explaining the distinction based on whether the return from the second buyer was by court judgment or by mutual agreement. The key principle is that if the buyer's own action (selling) makes the item impossible to return to the original seller, then he loses the right to return it. However, if a qadi's judgment nullifies the second sale retroactively, it is as if the buyer never sold it, so he may still return it to the original seller. Additionally, if the buyer sells after seeing the defect, that indicates acceptance of the defect, and he cannot return it. The proof is the athar from 'Amir, which is a strong textual evidence. This ruling is from the Hanafi school and is based on the concept of impediment (ta'azzur) caused by the buyer's action.

Key Terms
مبیع (mabī‘): The item sold in a contract of sale.
عیب (‘ayb): A defect or flaw in the item that existed at the time of sale and makes the item less valuable or undesirable.
قاضی (qāḍī): A judge who adjudicates disputes; in this context, his judgment can annul the second sale retroactively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the first buyer (Zayd) resells a defective slave to Khalid, and then Khalid returns the slave to Zayd without a court judgment, can Zayd return the slave to the original seller (Rahim)?
A) Yes, because the slave was defective at the time of the original sale.
B) No, because Zayd's sale to Khalid made return to the original seller impossible.
C) Yes, because Zayd can always return a defective item to his seller.
D) No, because the defect was not discovered until after the second sale.

Key Takeaway
A buyer cannot return a defective item to his seller if he resold it and the second sale was not annulled by a court, because his own action makes return impossible.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Stipulation of General Immunity from Defects in Sales
States the ruling when seller stipulates general immunity from defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on general immunity from defects, cite the primary evidence (hadith of 'Adi ibn Khalid and athar of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar), and evaluate the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
A general immunity clause covers all defects, even unnamed ones; the buyer cannot return the item unless the seller knowingly concealed the defect.

In sales, the seller may stipulate immunity from all defects (barā’a min kull ‘ayb). The Hanafi school holds that such a clause is valid and protects the seller from return claims for any defect, whether named or not. This lesson examines the ruling, its proofs from the Sunnah and Companion practice, and the disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on general immunity
From the passage, the ruling is that if the seller stipulates immunity from every defect, the buyer cannot return the item for any defect, even if defects were not named. Write down the ruling in one sentence.
2
Examine the hadith of 'Adi ibn Khalid
Read the hadith where the Prophet wrote a document for a sale with immunity from three specific categories. This is the primary proof. How does this support general immunity?
The hadith is from Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Book of Conditions, Hadith 1216.
3
Examine the athar of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar
Read the story where 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar sold a slave with general immunity. When a defect was discovered, 'Uthman ruled that 'Abdullah should swear he had no knowledge. This shows that general immunity was accepted.
From Muwatta Imam Malik, The Chapter on Defects in Slaves.
4
Understand the condition about the seller's knowledge
The immunity is valid only if the seller did not know of the defect. If he knew and concealed, the immunity does not protect him. Identify this condition in the text.
The text states: 'bisharteke ke aib ko jaante hue jhoot na bola ho'.
5
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that general immunity involves jahala (ignorance) and therefore only covers named defects. The Hanafi response is that the buyer had the opportunity to inspect, and the general stipulation is a valid condition. Note the thamarah al-khilaf.
Practical consequence: Under Hanafi, buyer cannot return; under Shafi'i, buyer can return for unnamed defects.

خالد بن هوذة من محمد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اشترى منى عبدا او امة لا داء ولا غائلة ولا خبثة بيع المسلم المسلم (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی کتابہ الشروط ص ۲۳۰ نمبر ۱۲۱۶) اس حدیث میں آپ نے لا جائے گا۔ بشرطیکہ عیب کو جانتے ہوئے جھوٹ نہ بولا ہو۔ اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ ان عبد الله بن عمر باع غلاما له بثماني مائة درهم فباعه بالبراءة فقال الذى ابتاعه لعبد الله بن عمر بالغلام داء لم تسمه لى بنانا ہے اس لئے اس میں جہالت نہیں چلے گی۔ اس لئے جن جن عیوب کا نام لے گا انہیں عیوب سے بری ہوگا۔ اور جن عیوب کا نام نہیں لے گا ان عیوب سے بائع بری نہیں ہوگا۔ ان عیوب کی وجہ سے مشتری کو مبیع لوٹانے کا حق ہوگا۔
(11) Someone bought a slave and the seller stipulated immunity from every defect. Then it is not permissible for the buyer to return it due to a defect, even if all defects were not named and were not enumerated. The seller made this sale and said: you look and buy; I am immune from all defects; then I will not accept return. So even if every [defect] is not named and all defects are not mentioned, still he will be immune from all defects. And the buyer cannot return it to the seller due to any defect. (1) The evidence for the validity of a sale with immunity from defects is this hadith: 'Adi ibn Khalid ibn Huwdha said to me: Shall I recite to you a letter that the Messenger of Allah wrote for me? I said yes. He brought out a letter: This is what 'Adi ibn Khalid ibn Huwdha bought from Muhammad, the Messenger of Allah. He bought from me a male slave or a female slave—no disease, no harm, no evil; the sale of a Muslim to a Muslim.' In this hadith, the Prophet wrote immunity from 'no disease, no harm, no evil' and gave it to the Companions, indicating that these defects will not be present. From this, it is understood that a sale with the condition of immunity from defects is permissible. And even if all defects were not enumerated, he will still be immune from all defects, provided that he did not knowingly lie about a defect. The evidence for this is this athar: 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar sold a slave of his for eight hundred dirhams and sold him with immunity. Then the buyer said to 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar: The slave has a disease you did not mention to me. They referred to 'Uthman ibn 'Affan. The man said: He sold me a slave and there is a disease in him he did not mention to me. 'Abdullah said: I sold him with immunity. 'Uthman ruled that 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar should swear that he sold him the slave and he did not know of any disease. 'Abdullah refused to swear, so the slave was returned to him. In this athar, 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar sold the slave with the condition of immunity from all defects and did not enumerate every defect. Therefore, 'Uthman accepted that, only requiring him to swear that he did not know of the defect at the time of sale. But 'Abdullah did not swear, so the slave was returned to him. This shows that when immunity from all defects is mentioned and every individual defect is not named, he will still be immune from all defects. (3) This athar is also evidence: From 'Abdullah ibn 'Amir from Zayd ibn Thabit that he considered immunity from every defect permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i says: Immunity from defects is like giving ownership of a good sale, so ignorance does not apply to it. Therefore, only for those defects that he names will he be immune; for those he does not name, the seller will not be immune. For those defects, the buyer has the right to return the item.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on stipulating general immunity from all defects (al-bara'a min kull 'ayb) in a sale. The ruling is that if the seller stipulates immunity from all defects, the buyer cannot return the item for any defect, even if the defects were not individually enumerated. The proof is the hadith of 'Adi ibn Khalid, where the Prophet wrote immunity from three specific categories, which is considered evidence that general immunity is valid. Additional evidence from the practice of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar and Zayd ibn Thabit supports this. The condition is that the seller did not knowingly conceal a defect he knew about; if he did, the immunity may not apply. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that immunity only covers named defects because it involves ownership with ignorance. The Hanafi position is that general immunity is valid because it is a known condition in the contract, and the buyer accepts the item as is. The commentary explains that the buyer's inspection (seeing) before purchase justifies the immunity, as the buyer can examine the item. This ruling is from the Hanafi school and is based on textual evidence from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions.

Key Terms
البراءة من كل عيب (al-barā’a min kull ‘ayb): A stipulation in a sale contract that the seller is immune from all defects in the item, meaning the buyer forfeits the right to return for any defect.
شرط البراءة (shart al-barā’a): The condition of immunity; a term inserted in the sale contract declaring exemption.
جہالت (jahāla): Ignorance or ambiguity; Shafi'i argues that general immunity involves jahala because the buyer doesn't know exactly what defects are included.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if the seller stipulates general immunity from all defects without naming them, can the buyer return the item for a defect that was not mentioned?
A) Yes, always.
B) Yes, if the defect is major.
C) No, because general immunity covers all defects.
D) No, but only if the seller didn't know.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a general immunity clause in a sale covers all defects, even unnamed ones, provided the seller did not fraudulently conceal a known defect.
