الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثانى )
كتاب البيوع
من ثوبين [ ۱۸۹۳ (۱۲) ومن باع عبدا على ان يعتقه المشترى او يدبره او یکاتبه او باع ان دو کپڑے مختلف انداز کے ہیں اور ایجاب کرتے وقت یہ نہیں بتا رہا ہے کہ دونوں میں سے کس کپڑے کی بیع ہورہی ہے، صرف یوں کہہ رہا ہے کہ دونوں کپڑوں میں سے ایک کی بیچ ہو رہی ہے تو چونکہ مبیع مجہول ہے بعد میں کپڑا سپرد کرنے میں جھگڑا ہوگا اس لئے یہ بیع فاسد ہوگی۔ حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ مجلس ختم ہونے سے پہلے ایک کپڑے کی تعیین ہو جائے تو بیع جائز ہو جائے گی۔
اصول مجہول مبیع کی بیع فاسد ہے۔ ۱۸۹۳ (۱۲) کسی نے غلام بیچا اس شرط پر کہ مشتری اس کو آزاد کرے گا یا اس کو مد بر بنائے گا یا اس کو مکاتب بنائے گا یا باندی بیچی اس شرط پر کہ
اس کو ام ولد بنائے گا تو بیع فاسد ہے۔ یہ مسائل اس اصول پر ہیں کہ بیچ کے ساتھ ایسی شرط لگائی جو بیچ کے موافق نہیں ہے تو وہ بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ شرط لگانے کی چار صورتیں ہیں (۱) ایسی شرط جو خود بیج کے موافق ہے، مثلا بیج اس لئے کرتا ہوں کہ مشتری کا قبضہ ہو جائے تو شرط خود بیع کا مقتضاء ہے اس لئے اس سے بیع فاسد نہیں ہوگی (۲) ایسی شرط لگائی جو بیع کے موافق نہیں ہے البتہ بائع کا فائدہ ہے، مثلا اس شرط پر گھر بیچتا ہوں کہ دو ماہ تک اس میں رہوں گا۔ اس صورت میں بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی (۳) اس شرط پر بیع کرے کہ مشتری کا فائدہ ہو مثلا اس شرط پر خریدتا ہوں کہ مجھے مزید قرض دیں گے۔ اس صورت میں بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی (۴) اور شرط کی چوتھی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایسی شرط لگائے جس میں خود مبیع کا فائدہ ہو اور بیع غلام یا باندی ہو جو قاضی کے قضا تک پہنچ سکتا ہو۔ اس صورت میں مبیع کا فائدہ ہے اور طبع جھگڑا کر سکتا ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی بیچ فاسد ہوگی۔ اوپر کا مسئلہ اسی چوتھی قسم کی شرط پر متفرع ہے۔ کیونکہ غلام کو آزاد کرنے ، اس کو مد بر بنانے اور اس کو مکاتب بنانے میں خود بیع کا فائدہ ہے اور مبیع انسان ہے اس لئے جھگڑا بھی کر سکتا ہے اس لئے بیع فاسد ہوگی۔ شریعت کے خلاف شرط لگانے سے حدیث میں منع فرمایا عن عائشة قالت ... ثم قال الله اما بعد ما بال رجال يشترطون شروطا ليست في كتاب الله ؟ ما كان من شرط ليس في كتاب الله فهو باطل وان كان مائة شرط قضاء الله احق وشرط الله اوثق (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا اشترط فی السبیع شروطالا تحل ص۲۹۰ نمبر ۲۱۶۸ ر مسلم شریف ، باب بیان ان الولاء لمن اعتق ج اول ص ۴۹۳ نمبر ۷/۱۵۰۴ ۳۷۷) اس حدیث میں بتایا گیا ہے شریعت کے خلاف جو بھی شرط لگائے اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہے (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے عبد الله بن عمر قال قال رسول الله الله لا يحل سلف و بيع ولا شرطان في بيع (ب) (ابو
داؤد شریف، باب فی الرجل بیچ مالیس عندہ ج ثانی ص ۱۳۹ نمبر ۳۵۰۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دوشرطیں لگانا ممنوع ہے۔ اور خاص طور پر جس شرط لگانے سے جھگڑے کا خطرہ ہو اس سے بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا امابعد لوگوں کو کیا ہوا کہ شرط لگاتے ہیں ایسی شرط جو اللہ کی کتاب میں نہیں ہے، جو شرط اللہ کی کتاب میں نہ ہو تو وہ باطل ہے اگر چہ سو شرطیں ہوں۔ اللہ کا فیصلہ زیادہ حقدار ہے اور اللہ کی شریا زیادہ مضبوط ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا نہیں حلال ہے ادھار بیچنا اور بیع کرنا اور نہ دو شرطیں ایک بیع میں ۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثاني
كتاب البيوع
امة على ان يستولدها فالبيع فاسد [۸۹۴] (۱۳) و کذلک لو باع عبدا على ان يستخدمه البائع شهرا او دارا على ان يسكنها البائع مدة معلومة او على ان يقرضه المشترى درهما
انوان ایسی شرط جو بیج کے مخالف ہو اور بائع یا مشتری یا مبیع کا فائدہ ہو اور مبیع انسان ہو تو اس سے بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اس میں انسان کا فطری فائدہ ہے اس لئے ایسی شرط لگا کر بیچنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ حضرت عائشہ نے حضرت بریرہ کو آزاد کرنے کی شرط سے خریدا تھا جیسا کہ او پر حدیث گزری (بخاری شریف، نمبر ۱۲۱۶۸ مسلم شریف نمبر ۱۵۰۴)
ید بره : مدیر بنادے، مولی غلام سے کہے کہ تم میرے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہو۔ یکا تبہ : مکاتب بنائے، مولی غلام سے کہے کہ اتنے روپے ادا کرو تو تم آزاد ہو جاؤ گے اس کو مکاتب بنانا کہتے ہیں۔ لیستو لدھا : ام ولد بنائے ، باندی سے ولی کرے پھر اس سے مولی کا بچہ پیدا ہو تو اس کی ماں یعنی باندی ام ولد ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور مولی کے مرنے کے بعد وہ آزاد ہو جائے گی ۔ ایسی باندی کو ام ولد کہتے ہیں۔ ۸۹۴] (۱۳) ایسے ہی غلام بیچا اس شرط پر کہ اس سے بائع ایک ماہ تک خدمت لے گا یا گھر بیچا اس شرط پر کہ اس میں بائع ایک مدت معلوم تک ٹھہرے گا یا اس شرط پر کہ مشتری اس کو کچھ درہم قرض دے گا یا اس شرط پر کہ مشتری اس کو ہدیہ دے گا تو بیع فاسد ہے۔ این عبارت میں چار مسئلے بیان کئے گئے ہیں۔ اور چاروں بیوع کے فاسد ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ بائع بیع کے خلاف شرطیں لگا رہا ہے جس میں بائع کا فائدہ ہے اور پہلے اصول گزر چکا ہے کہ بیچ کے خلاف شرط ہو اور بائع یا مشتری کا فائدہ ہو تو بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ مثلا بائع نے غلام بیچا اس شرط پر کہ غلام ایک ماہ تک بائع کی خدمت کرے گا تو بیع فاسد ہوگی۔ کیونکہ غلام تو بکتے ہی مشتری کا ہو جائے گا تو بائع کی خدمت کیوں کرے؟ یا اس شرط پر گھر بچا کہ بائع اس میں ایک مدت معلوم مثلا ایک ماہ تک مقیم رہے گا۔ یا اس شرط پر بیچا کہ مشتری بائع کو کچھ پونڈ قرض دے گا یا ہدیہ دیگا تو یہ شرطیں فاسد ہیں اس لئے ان سے بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ اس اثر سے بھی خدمت کی شرط لگانے کی ممانعت معلوم ہوتی ہے ان عمر ابن الخطاب اعطى امرأة عبد الله بن مسعود جارية من الخمس فباعتها من عبد الله بن مسعود بالف درهم واشترطت عليها خدمتها فبلغ عمر بن خطاب فقال يا ابا عبد الرحمن اشتريت جارية امرأتک فاشترطت عليك خدمتها فقال نعم فقال لا تشترها وفيها مثنوية (سنن ليحقى ، باب من باع حیوانا اوغیرہ و استثنی منافعہ مدة ج خامس ص ۵۴۹، نمبر ۱۰۸۳۵) حدیث اور اصول پہلے گزر چکے ہیں۔ اس مسئلہ میں بائع کے فائدے کی شرط ہے اس لئے بیع فاسد ہوگی۔ ال بعض حضرات کی رائے ہے کہ ایسی شرط پر بائع اور مشتری راضی ہو جائیں تو جائز ہے۔
حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے جابر بن عبد اللہ سے اونٹ خریدا اور حضرت نے شرط لگائی کہ گھر تک اس پر سوار ہو کر جاؤں گا پھر اونٹ آپ کے حوالے کروں گا۔ حدثنی جابر بن عبد اللـه انـه كـان يسير على جمل له قد اعيا ... ثم قال بعنيه فبعته بوقية و استثنيت عليه حملانه الى اهلي فلما بلغت اتيته بالجمل فنقدني ثمنه (الف) ( مسلم شریف، باب البغیر واستثناء رکو به ج ثانی
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت جابر بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ ایک اونٹ پر سوار تھے جو تھک چکا تھا۔ پھر آپ نے فرمایا اس اونٹ کو میرے ہاتھ بیچ دو۔ حضرت فرماتے ہیں کہ چالیس درہم میں میں نے اس کو بیچ دیا اور میرے اہل یعنی مدینہ تک اس پر سوار ہونا مستثنی کر لیا۔ پس جب مدینہ پہنچا تو اونٹ لیکر آپ کے (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
The commentary continues on the book of sales. (12) [1893] And whoever sells a slave on condition that the buyer frees him, or makes him mudabbar, or makes him mukatib, or sells a slave-girl on condition that he makes her umm walad, the sale is fasid. The principle: the sale of an unknown object (majhul) is fasid. These cases are based on the principle that when a condition is attached to a sale that is contrary to the nature of the sale, the sale becomes fasid. There are four types of conditions: (1) a condition that is consistent with the sale itself, e.g., the sale is for the buyer to take possession—this does not make it fasid; (2) a condition contrary to the sale but beneficial to the seller, e.g., selling a house on condition that the seller lives in it for two months—this makes it fasid; (3) a condition for the buyer's benefit, e.g., buying on condition that the seller gives him a loan—fasid; (4) a condition for the benefit of the object sold itself, and the object is a slave or slave-girl who can reach the judge for litigation. This also makes the sale fasid. The above case (slave freed etc.) falls under this fourth type. This is prohibited by hadith: Aisha narrated that the Prophet said, 'What is the matter with people who stipulate conditions that are not in the Book of Allah? Any condition not in the Book of Allah is invalid, even if it were a hundred conditions. The decree of Allah is more deserving and the condition of Allah is more binding.' (Bukhari, Muslim). Also, Ibn Umar narrated that the Prophet forbade a sale with a loan and two conditions in one sale. (Abu Dawud). (13) [894] Similarly, if one sells a slave on condition that the seller uses his service for a month, or a house on condition that the seller resides in it for a known period, or on condition that the buyer lends him a dirham, or gives him a gift, the sale is fasid. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that this is permissible because it is a natural benefit for the human. But the correct view is that it is fasid due to the condition contrary to the sale. The narration of Umar ibn al-Khattab regarding the wife of Ibn Mas'ud selling a slave-girl from the khums and stipulating her service supports this prohibition. Some hold that if both parties agree, it is permissible. However, the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah where he sold a camel to the Prophet on condition that he ride it to his family shows that such conditions are permissible in certain contexts (but that is an exception).
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samari is an expansion on the rulings of conditions in sales (shurut fi al-bay'). The author begins by stating the well-known Hanafi principle: the sale of a majhul (unknown) object is fasid. He then presents a series of cases from the matn: selling a slave on condition that the buyer frees him, makes him mudabbar, or mukatib, or selling a slave-girl on condition that the buyer makes her umm walad. These are all examples of conditions that are contrary to the nature of the sale. The author categorizes conditions into four types: (1) conditions that are part of the sale's requirement (e.g., delivery), which do not invalidate the sale; (2) conditions that benefit the seller but are not part of the sale (e.g., seller retains usufruct), which invalidate; (3) conditions that benefit the buyer but are not part of the sale (e.g., additional loan), which invalidate; (4) conditions that benefit the object itself when the object is a human capable of litigation (e.g., freeing a slave), which also invalidate because the object can itself claim a right. The author then supports the ruling with two hadith: the first from Aisha that any condition not in Allah's Book is invalid, and the second from Ibn Umar prohibiting two conditions in one sale. He also cites the incident of Umar forbidding the purchase of a slave-girl with a condition of her service. Importantly, the author addresses the Shafi'i position that such conditions are permissible based on the precedent of Aisha buying Barirah with the condition of freeing her (which Shafi'is interpret as a valid condition). The Hanafi response is that the condition freeing the slave is actually for the benefit of the object itself, which falls under the fourth category, but the Shafi'i view is distinguished. The passage also discusses another set of examples (mas'ala 13): selling a slave with condition of service to the seller, selling a house with seller's right to reside, or conditional loan/gift. All are declared fasid. The author notes that some scholars allow if both parties agree, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is fasid. The hadith of Jabir selling the camel with the condition of riding it to his family is mentioned as a potential exception (istisna'), which is a separate discussion. Overall, the commentary emphasizes that conditions contradicting the essence of the sale (muqawim) lead to fasid, and the evidence from the Sunnah and rational reasoning (qiyas) is clear.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition stipulated in a contract that is not inherent to its nature; here, a condition that contradicts the sale's essence.
مبيح مجهول (mabii' majhul): An unknown object of sale that causes uncertainty (gharar), leading to fasid.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who is promised freedom upon the master's death; the condition here is that the buyer makes him mudabbar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person sells his house on the condition that he himself will live in it for one month after the sale, what is the ruling?
A) The sale is valid and the condition is binding.
B) The sale is valid but the condition is void.
C) The sale is fasid (voidable) because the condition is contrary to the nature of the sale and benefits the seller.
D) The sale is batil (void) because the condition is forbidden.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, any condition not inherent to the sale's nature that introduces benefit or uncertainty invalidates the contract to restore clarity.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Sale Invalid Due to Conflicting Conditions
Ruling on conflicting conditions benefiting seller/buyer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditions contrary to sale and apply the principle to identify a fasid sale.

Core Idea
A condition that contradicts the sale and benefits one party makes the sale fasid — even if both agree.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rule that certain conditions invalidate a sale. When a stipulation (shart) contradicts the immediate transfer of ownership and benefits the seller or buyer, the sale becomes fasid (voidable). Through examples from classical texts, we learn to distinguish valid from invalid conditions, and understand the evidence and ikhtilaf involved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? What is the hukm? Here, the act is a sale with an additional condition. The ruling is fasid (voidable).
Fasid means the sale does not transfer ownership unless the condition is removed.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith of Umar forbidding purchase of a slave-girl with a service condition, and the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet allowed riding the camel home (which some use as evidence for permissibility).
The Hanafi rely on the general prohibition of conditions that contradict the sale.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does the dalil prove the ruling? The hadith of Umar explicitly says 'Do not buy her [with] a condition' — showing that such conditions are prohibited. The Jabir hadith is distinguished as a special permission.
The Hanafi argue that the default is invalidity unless proven otherwise.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? The Shafi'i school considers such conditions valid, citing the hadith of 'Aisha and Barira.
The Hanafi respond that Barira's condition was about wala', not the sale itself.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The Hanafi position (fasid) is mufta bihi; mutual consent does not cure the defect.
Some later Hanafi scholars allow if both parties agree, but the majority view is fasid.

ید بره : مدیر بنادے، مولی غلام سے کہے کہ تم میرے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہو۔ یکا تبہ : مکاتب بنائے، مولی غلام سے کہے کہ اتنے روپے ادا کرو تو تم آزاد ہو جاؤ گے اس کو مکاتب بنانا کہتے ہیں۔ لیستو لدھا : ام ولد بنائے ، باندی سے ولی کرے پھر اس سے مولی کا بچہ پیدا ہو تو اس کی ماں یعنی باندی ام ولد ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور مولی کے مرنے کے بعد وہ آزاد ہو جائے گی ۔ ایسی باندی کو ام ولد کہتے ہیں۔ ۸۹۴] (۱۳) ایسے ہی غلام بیچا اس شرط پر کہ اس سے بائع ایک ماہ تک خدمت لے گا یا گھر بیچا اس شرط پر کہ اس میں بائع ایک مدت معلوم تک ٹھہرے گا یا اس شرط پر کہ مشتری اس کو کچھ درہم قرض دے گا یا اس شرط پر کہ مشتری اس کو ہدیہ دے گا تو بیع فاسد ہے۔ این عبارت میں چار مسئلے بیان کئے گئے ہیں۔ اور چاروں بیوع کے فاسد ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ بائع بیع کے خلاف شرطیں لگا رہا ہے جس میں بائع کا فائدہ ہے اور پہلے اصول گزر چکا ہے کہ بیچ کے خلاف شرط ہو اور بائع یا مشتری کا فائدہ ہو تو بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ مثلا بائع نے غلام بیچا اس شرط پر کہ غلام ایک ماہ تک بائع کی خدمت کرے گا تو بیع فاسد ہوگی۔ کیونکہ غلام تو بکتے ہی مشتری کا ہو جائے گا تو بائع کی خدمت کیوں کرے؟ یا اس شرط پر گھر بچا کہ بائع اس میں ایک مدت معلوم مثلا ایک ماہ تک مقیم رہے گا۔ یا اس شرط پر بیچا کہ مشتری بائع کو کچھ پونڈ قرض دے گا یا ہدیہ دیگا تو یہ شرطیں فاسد ہیں اس لئے ان سے بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ اس اثر سے بھی خدمت کی شرط لگانے کی ممانعت معلوم ہوتی ہے ان عمر ابن الخطاب اعطى امرأة عبد الله بن مسعود جارية من الخمس فباعتها من عبد الله بن مسعود بالف درهم واشترطت عليها خدمتها فبلغ عمر بن خطاب فقال یا ابا عبد الرحمن اشتريت جارية امرأتک فاشترطت عليك خدمتها فقال نعم فقال لا تشترها وفيها مثنوية (سنن ليحقى ، باب من باع حیوانا اوغیرہ و استثنی منافعہ مدة ج خامس ص ۵۴۹، نمبر ۱۰۸۳۵) حدیث اور اصول پہلے گزر چکے ہیں۔ اس مسئلہ میں بائع کے فائدے کی شرط ہے اس لئے بیع فاسد ہوگی۔ ال بعض حضرات کی رائے ہے کہ ایسی شرط پر بائع اور مشتری راضی ہو جائیں تو جائز ہے۔

حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے جابر بن عبد اللہ سے اونٹ خریدا اور حضرت نے شرط لگائی کہ گھر تک اس پر سوار ہو کر جاؤں گا پھر اونٹ آپ کے حوالے کروں گا۔ حدثنی جابر بن عبد اللـه انـه كـان يسير على جمل له قد اعيا ... ثم قال بعنيه فبعته بوقية و استثنيت عليه حملانه الى اهلي فلما بلغت اتيته بالجمل فنقدني ثمنه (الف) ( مسلم شریف، باب البغیر واستثناء رکو به ج ثانی

حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت جابر بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ ایک اونٹ پر سوار تھے جو تھک چکا تھا۔ پھر آپ نے فرمایا اس اونٹ کو میرے ہاتھ بیچ دو۔ حضرت فرماتے ہیں کہ چالیس درہم میں میں نے اس کو بیچ دیا اور میرے اہل یعنی مدینہ تک اس پر سوار ہونا مستثنی کر لیا۔ پس جب مدینہ پہنچا تو اونٹ لیکر آپ کے (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )

نمبر ۴۰۹۸/۱۲۰۰) اس حدیث میں حضرت جابر نے اونٹ بیچا اور اس کی خدمت مدینہ تک سوار ہونے کی اپنے لئے مخصوص کی۔ اور حضور نے جائزہ کیا اس لئے بائع اور مشتری راضی ہو جائیں تو ایسی شرط سے بیع فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔
If he sells a female slave on condition that he will have children with her, the sale is fasid. Similarly, if he sells a slave on condition that the seller uses his service for a month, or a house on condition that the seller resides in it for a known period, or on condition that the buyer gives him a loan... [Urdu commentary follows explaining the ruling, Shafi'i's opinion, and the hadith of Jabir.]
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a sale is fasid if it includes a condition that contradicts the essence of the sale and benefits the seller or buyer. The matn gives examples: selling a slave-girl with the condition of istiwlad (making her umm walad), selling a slave with a condition of service, a house with a condition of residence, or a condition of a loan from the buyer. The commentary explains that such conditions are invalid because they conflict with the immediate transfer of ownership. The Shafi'i position is mentioned: they consider such conditions permissible, citing the hadith of 'Aisha buying Barira with a condition of wala'. The Hanafi response relies on the principle that conditions contrary to sale are invalid. The hadith of Jabir about selling a camel with the condition of riding it home is discussed, and some scholars consider mutual consent as valid. However, the relied-upon position is that such conditions make the sale fasid.

Key Terms
بيوع (buyu'): Sales, plural of bay'
فاسد (fasid): Voidable sale that does not transfer ownership unless conditions are removed
شرط (shart): A stipulation in the contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, if someone sells a house on condition that the seller lives in it for a month, the sale is:
A) Valid (sahih)
B) Voidable (fasid)
C) Void (batil)
D) Suspended (mawquf)

Key Takeaway
A condition that contradicts the essence of sale and benefits one party makes the sale fasid, even if both parties consent.

Sale Invalidated by Condition of Gift
Matn ruling on sale with gift condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale conditioned on a gift and explain why the condition renders the sale fasid.

Core Idea
A sale is fasid if the seller stipulates an extra benefit not integral to the contract.

In Hanafi fiqh, the essence of a sale is the exchange of commodity for price. Any condition that adds an extra benefit to one party and is not naturally part of the transaction corrupts the contract. This lesson examines the matn that declares a sale fasid when the buyer is required to give a gift to the seller.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a sale (bay') with an added condition (shart) that the buyer gives a gift (hadiyya) to the seller. The ruling is that the sale is fasid (defective).
Fasid means the contract is valid in its essence but invalid due to an external defect.
2
Understand the reason for fasid
The condition is not part of the consideration (commodity or price). It gives the seller an extra benefit uncorrelated to the value, resembling riba or gharar. Hanafi usul: any condition that is not in the covenant (qarar) and confers only a benefit on one party invalidates the contract.
This is based on the hadith: 'Muslims are bound by their conditions, except a condition that permits the prohibited or prohibits the permitted.'
3
Distinguish from valid conditions
Conditions that are integral to the sale (like payment terms, delivery time, or option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart)) are valid. The gift condition is extraneous and purely beneficial to the seller.
The option of stipulation is a condition that suspends the contract, not an extra exchange.
4
Apply to similar cases
Any condition that gives a unilateral benefit to one party without corresponding consideration causes fasd. Examples: buyer stipulates seller must provide free delivery (if not customary), or seller requires buyer to lend him money.
Customary conditions ('urf) may be excepted, but the gift condition is not customary.

Source Text

او على ان يهدى له [۸۹۵] (۱۴)

(۸۹۵) (۱۳) کسی نے کوئی مینی چیز بیچی اس شرط پر کہ اس کو ایک مہینے میں سپر د کرے گا تو بیع فاسد ہے۔
Or on condition that he gives a gift to him. [895] (14)

(895) (13) Someone sold a specific thing on condition that he will deliver it after a month, the sale is fasid.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage contains the matn stating that selling with a condition that the buyer gives a gift to the seller renders the sale fasid. However, the commentary provided seems to be mismatched with the ruling on delayed delivery (15). According to the earlier principle, a condition that benefits the seller (like receiving a gift) and conflicts with the sale is invalid.

Key Terms
بيع فاسد (bay' fasid): A defective sale that is valid in essence but invalid due to an external condition; can be rectified.
شرط (shart): A condition or stipulation in a contract.
هدية (hadiyya): Gift; an extra transfer of ownership without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, what is the ruling on a sale where the seller stipulates that the buyer give him a gift?
A) Valid because the condition is a separate transaction
B) Fasid because the condition is an extra benefit
C) Batil because gifts are prohibited in sales
D) Makruh but valid

Key Takeaway
A sale conditioned on the buyer giving a gift to the seller is fasid because it imposes an extraneous benefit on the seller, violating the principle that a sale must be free of such conditions.

Bay' 'Ayn: Invalid Condition of Deferred Delivery
Ruling on condition of deferred delivery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a seller stipulates delayed delivery in a sale of a present item and explain why the sale becomes fasid.

Core Idea
A sale of a present item requires immediate delivery; any condition delaying delivery makes the sale fasid.

In Hanafi fiqh, selling a specific, present item (bay' 'ayn) transfers ownership instantly. Including a condition to deliver the item at a future date contradicts the nature of the contract and benefits the seller improperly. This lesson explores why such a condition renders the sale fasid (invalid) and distinguishes it from the valid sale of salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction
Recognize that the passage discusses bay' 'ayn, a sale of a specific, present item. Ownership transfers immediately upon contract, unlike salam where delivery is deferred.
The key is that the item is present and owned by the seller at the time of sale.
2
Locate the invalid condition
The condition is that the seller will deliver the item after a specified period (e.g., one month). This condition is separate from the main contract.
The condition benefits the seller by allowing him to keep the item longer, which is against the nature of bay' 'ayn.
3
Apply the ruling
Such a condition is fasid (invalid) and causes the entire sale to be fasid. The sale is voidable; the buyer may rescind or renegotiate.
Fasid means the sale is temporarily invalid and can be rectified by removing the condition.
4
Understand the dalil
The hadith of Jabir (Abu Dawud) prohibits similar practices (bai' al-sinin and exceptions). It shows that stipulating future delivery in an immediate sale is forbidden.
The hadith is ahad with zanni thubut and dalala, but it is sufficient to make the sale fasid.
5
Distinguish from salam
In salam, deferred delivery is allowed because the item is not present and the price is paid in advance. In bay' 'ayn, the item is present, so immediate delivery is required.
Salam has strict conditions: full payment at contract, specified description, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن باع عينا على ان يسلمها الى رأس الشهر فالبيع فاسد [ ۸۹۶] (۱۵)

تشريح ایک ہے بیع سلم اس میں مبیع مہینوں کے بعد دی جاتی ہے لیکن یہ فوری بیج ہے۔ مبیع سامنے موجود ہے جس کو بیع عین کہتے ہیں۔ اس میں جیسے ہی بیع ہوئی مشتری بیع کا مالک بن گیا۔ اس لئے اب یہ شرط لگانا کہ ایک مہینے کے بعد مبیع سپرد کریں گے شرط فاسد ہے اور بائع کا اس میں فائدہ ہے اس لئے بیع فاسد ہوگی۔ اس حدیث میں اس کی ممانعت ہے عن جابر بن عبد الله قال نهى رسول الله له عن المحاقلة ... وقال آخر بيع السنين ثم اتفقوا وعن التنيا (الف) (ابوداء وشريف، باب فی التخابر ق ص ۱۲۷ نمبر ۳۴۰۴) عین : بیع سلم کے خلاف فوری بیع۔ راس الشهر : مہینے کے شروع میں یا ایک مینہ پر۔
And whoever sells a specific thing on condition that he delivers it at the beginning of the month, the sale is fasid. [896] (15)

Explanation: Bay' salam is when the object is delivered after months, but this is an immediate sale. The object is present, called bay' 'ayn. As soon as the sale is made, the buyer becomes owner. So stipulating delivery after a month is an invalid condition benefiting the seller, making the sale fasid. The hadith prohibits this.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage rules that selling a specific, present item with a condition of deferred delivery (e.g., after one month) makes the sale fasid. The commentary distinguishes between bay' salam (deferred delivery) and bay' 'ayn (immediate delivery). In bay' 'ayn, ownership transfers instantly, so a condition postponing delivery is contrary to the contract. The hadith of Jabir prohibiting bai' al-sinin (selling with deferred years) supports this. The condition benefits the seller by allowing him to keep the item, thus invalidating the sale.

Key Terms
عين ('ayn): Specific, present item being sold
سلم (salam): Sale with advance payment and deferred delivery

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is selling a present item with deferred delivery fasid?
A) Because the buyer cannot take possession
B) Because ownership transfers instantly, so delaying delivery is against the contract
C) Because the price is unknown
D) Because the seller must guarantee the item

Key Takeaway
Selling a present item with a condition of delayed delivery is fasid because ownership transfers immediately; the condition is contrary to the contract and benefits the seller.

Sale Invalid with Exception of Fetus or Cutting
Rulings on selling with exception of fetus or tailoring

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions that render a sale fasid under Hanafi law, specifically when a thunaya (exception) or an additional service condition is included.

Core Idea
Excluding an unborn fetus from a sale or adding a tailoring condition invalidates the sale — such exceptions make it fasid.

A sale must transfer full ownership of the object without ambiguity. If the seller tries to exclude part of the object (like the fetus of a pregnant animal) or imposes an extra obligation (like cutting cloth into a garment), the contract becomes fasid. This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on these two scenarios and the underlying proof from Hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on two transactions: selling a pregnant slave/animal with the fetus excluded, and buying cloth with a condition that the seller cuts it into a specific garment. In both cases, the sale is declared fasid (voidable).
Fasid means the contract is defective due to an invalid condition but can be corrected by removing the condition.
2
Analyze the invalidating condition
The condition that invalidates the sale is the thunaya (exception) — excluding a part of the object that is not separately defined, or adding a service that benefits the buyer beyond the mere sale.
In Hanafi law, the object of sale must be known and deliverable. The fetus is part of the mother until birth, so excluding it creates uncertainty (gharar).
3
Connect to the proof (dalil)
The Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) prohibited thunaya (exceptions in sales). This hadith, though ahad, is used by Hanafis to declare such sales fasid.
The prohibition is general; any sale containing a prohibited thunaya becomes fasid.
4
Understand the practical consequence
If the sale is fasid, it is not valid until the invalid condition is removed. If possession has been taken, the buyer must return the item or renegotiate without the condition.
This differs from batil (void) sales which cannot be corrected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن باع جارية او دابة الا حملها فسد البيع [۸۹۷] (١٦) ومن

(۸۹۷) (١٦) کسی نے کپڑا خریدا اس شرط پر کہ بائع اس کو کاٹ دیگا اور اس کا قمیص ہی دے گا یا قبای دے گا، یا چپل خریدی اس شرط پر کہ اس کو برابر کر دے گا یا پٹی لگا دے گا تو بیع فاسد ہوگی۔ تشریح کپڑا خریدا اور یہ بھی شرط لگائی کہ بائع اس کو کاٹ کر قمیص کسی دیگ یا قباسی دیگا تو خرید نے کے علاوہ یہ الگ شرط ہے جس میں مشتری کا مطلب ہے
And whoever sells a slave-girl or riding animal except its pregnancy, the sale is fasid. [897] (16) And whoever...

(897) (16) Someone bought cloth on condition that the seller cuts it and gives it as a shirt or robe, or bought sandals on condition that he levels them or straps them, the sale is fasid. Explanation: The condition of cutting is separate and benefits the buyer.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage covers two scenarios: (1) Selling a pregnant female slave or animal with the condition that the pregnancy is excluded makes the sale fasid, because the fetus is part of the mother until birth. (2) Buying cloth with the condition that the seller cuts it into a garment also makes the sale fasid, as it is an additional condition benefiting the buyer. The hadith prohibits such exceptions (thunaya).

Key Terms
ثنيا (thunaya): Making an exception in a sale, e.g., excluding part of the item

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the status of a sale when a buyer purchases cloth under the condition that the seller cuts it into a shirt?
A) The sale is valid because the price is agreed.
B) The sale is fasid because of an additional condition.
C) The sale is batil because the object is undefined.
D) The sale is valid if the buyer pays extra.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a sale that includes an exception of an inseparable part (thunaya) or an additional condition benefiting one party is fasid and must be corrected.

Sale with Condition to Deliver at Month's End: Ruling and Proof
Ruling and proof for a sale conditioned on future delivery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a spot sale with a condition to defer delivery and explain the proof from hadith and the distinction from salam.

Core Idea
A condition benefiting the seller in a spot sale voids the sale — ownership transfers instantly.

In Hanafi fiqh, a spot sale (bay' al-'ayn) requires immediate transfer of ownership. If the seller adds a condition to deliver later, that condition contradicts the essence of the contract and benefits the seller, making the sale fasid. This lesson examines the ruling and the proof from the hadith of Jabir, and clarifies why this is not a valid salam sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling a specific present item (bay' al-'ayn) with a condition to deliver at the beginning of the month. Ruling: the sale is fasid.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet (saw) forbade certain conditional sales (thunaya).
Refer to the hadith reference in the source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition implies that any condition not in harmony with the contract's nature (like deferring delivery in a spot sale) renders it void.
4
Distinguish from salam
Salam allows deferred delivery because it is a separate contract type with its own rules; here the item is present, so ownership transfers immediately.
Salam requires advance payment and specified future delivery.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may allow such conditions if mutually agreed, but Hanafi considers it fasid due to gharar and benefit to seller.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is the validity of the contract.

The author distinguishes it from salam, where deferred delivery is allowed. Because ownership transfers instantly in a spot sale, a condition to deliver later is void (fasid). The proof is from the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet forbade certain conditional sales. The key terms are explained: 'ayn (immediate sale) and ra's al-shahr (beginning of the month).

Selling an Animal Excluding Its Foetus: Hanafi Ruling
Ruling and proof for excluding the unborn foetus from a sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on excluding the unborn foetus from a sale and explain the legal basis using the hadith prohibition of thunaya.

Core Idea
Excluding the foetus is invalid; it is part of the mother until birth.

In Hanafi fiqh, the unborn foetus of a female animal or slave-girl is legally considered a part of its mother as long as it is in the womb. Therefore, when the mother is sold, the foetus is automatically included. Any condition to exclude it renders the sale fasid (void). This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is selling a female animal (or slave-girl) with a condition excluding her unborn foetus. The ruling is that the sale becomes fasid (void).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah (RA) in which the Prophet (SAW) forbade making exceptions (thunaya) in sales, except for 'araya. This prohibition includes invalid conditions that exclude part of the subject matter.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'thunaya' refers to exceptions or stipulations that exclude something. Since the foetus is part of the mother, excluding it is a thunaya that contradicts the completeness of the sale. Hence the prohibition applies.
4
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
Although some schools may allow clear stipulations to exclude the foetus, the Hanafi school considers it fasid due to gharar (uncertainty) and the unity of mother and foetus in sales.
In inheritance and bequest, the foetus is treated separately, but that exception does not apply in sales.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Consider a person selling a pregnant cow and saying 'I sell the cow but not its calf'. The calf is unborn, so the condition is void and the entire sale is fasid.
The seller must either include the calf or renegotiate the contract.

(15) And whoever sells a slave-girl or an animal except its unborn foetus, the sale is void. Explanation: He sold the slave-girl but said 'except her foetus' — he excluded it from the sale. Similarly, selling an animal excluding its foetus makes the sale void. (1) The foetus before birth is like a part of the mother, so selling the mother includes selling its parts. Hence the condition to exclude the foetus is void. (2) The hadith of Jabir: the Prophet forbade... and granted concession in 'araya. This shows that an un-Islamic exclusion is invalid. Note: In inheritance and bequest, the foetus is considered separate.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on selling a female animal (slave-girl or beast) with the condition that her unborn foetus is excluded. The Hanafi position is that such a condition makes the sale fasid (void) because the foetus is legally considered a part of the mother until birth. Therefore, selling the mother includes the foetus, and excluding it is a void condition (shart fasid). The proof is from the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet forbade making exceptions (thunaya) in sales, except for 'araya. The text also notes an exception: in inheritance and bequest, the foetus is treated separately, but that does not affect sales.

Key Terms

حمل (haml): The unborn foetus of an animal or slave-girl.

Excluding an unborn foetus from the sale of its mother is invalid (fasid) because the foetus is considered part of the mother in Hanafi fiqh.

Sale with Condition of Service: Fasid Unless Customary
Ruling with proof for sale plus service condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale with a condition of tailoring and apply the custom exception ('urf) to determine validity.

Core Idea
A sale with a service condition is fasid unless the condition is customary in the market.

When a buyer requires the seller to cut and sew cloth into a garment, or to shape and strap sandals, this combines a sale with a hire (ijarah) in one contract. The Hanafi school deems such a sale fasid (void) because it falls under the prohibited 'two sales in one' transaction. However, an important exception is made for local custom: if it is standard practice to sell sandals ready-fitted, the sale is valid. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the role of custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on the sale with a condition
Read the passage to determine the default hukm when a cloth or sandal is sold with a condition that the seller performs additional work (cutting, sewing, shaping).
The ruling is explicitly given as 'fasid' (void).
2
Understand the reason: two contracts in one
Realise that the condition of service constitutes a separate hire contract (ijarah) embedded within the sale. Combining two contracts in one transaction is prohibited by the hadith 'two sales in one'.
The text equates this to 'bay'atan fi bay'ah'.
3
Recognise the exception: local custom ('urf)
Note that the passage adds an exception: in countries where selling sandals already shaped and strapped is customary, the sale is valid. Custom can override the general prohibition.
Custom (ta'aruf) makes the condition acceptable because it does not surprise the parties.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a modern scenario: buying a suit with a condition that the tailor also alters it. Determine whether the sale is fasid or valid based on market custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(16) If someone buys cloth on condition that the seller cuts and sews it into a shirt or cloak, or buys sandals on condition that the seller shapes them or straps them, the sale is void. Explanation: The buyer imposes an additional condition of service (tailoring) which benefits the buyer. It was already stated that a condition benefiting either party against the nature of the contract voids the sale. Here the buyer benefits, so the sale is void. This combines a sale with a hire (ijarah) in one contract, resembling two sales in one. The hadith of Abu Hurairah prohibits two sales in one. Hence the sale is void. However, in some countries where it is customary to sell sandals already fitted, the sale is valid due to custom. Key terms: na'l (shoe/sandal), hazwa (shaping), tashreek (strapping).
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage discusses a sale where the buyer requires the seller to perform additional work—cutting and sewing cloth into a garment, or shaping and strapping sandals. The Hanafi ruling is that such a condition makes the sale fasid because it combines a sale (of the cloth) with a service (hiring of the seller's labor) in a single contract, which is akin to two transactions in one (bay'atan fi bay'ah), prohibited by hadith. The condition benefits the buyer, which also violates the principle that conditions contrary to the contract's nature void it. However, an important exception is made for customary practice: in regions where it is normal to sell sandals already fitted, the sale is valid because the custom ('urf) overrides the general prohibition. The text defines key terms: na'l (shoe), hazwa (cutting to shape), tashreek (attaching straps).

Key Terms
نعل (na'l): Shoe or sandal.
حذو (hazwa): Shaping or cutting a sandal to fit the foot.
تشرك (tashreek): Attaching straps to a sandal.
بيعتين في بيعة (bay'atan fi bay'ah): 'Two sales in one' – a prohibited transaction where a single contract contains two distinct sales or a sale and another contract.
عرف ('urf): Custom or established practice in a locality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A sale with a condition of service is fasid by default, but local custom ('urf) can make it valid.

Sale to an Unknown Future Date: The Hanafi Ruling on Uncertain Terms
Ruling and proof for sale with unspecified future time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a sale with an unknown term, explain why it is fasid, and cite the hadith evidence from Ibn 'Abbas.

Core Idea
A sale with an unknown future term is void (fasid) because the time must be definite to prevent dispute.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on sales where the time of delivery or payment is set to an indeterminate future event, such as a festival whose exact date is unknown. You will learn why such a contract is void (fasid) and how the hadith on salam establishes the requirement of a known term.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sale (bay') where the term (ajal) is set to an unknown future date, e.g., 'I sell on the day of Nowruz' without knowing when Nowruz occurs. The ruling: the sale is fasid (void).
Fasid means the contract is defective and does not transfer ownership; it must be rescinded unless the defect is cured.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: the Prophet (ﷺ) said, 'Do not advance salam in fruits until a known measure and a known term.' This hadith, though specifically about salam, establishes the general principle that a known term is required in deferred contracts.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim, graded sahih.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command to specify a known term (ajal ma'lum) implies that an unknown term invalidates the contract. The reasoning is that uncertainty in time leads to gharar (excessive risk) and potential dispute.
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) generally indicates obligation unless there is evidence to the contrary. Here, the term is obligatory for validity.
4
Note cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i, Maliki) may permit such a sale if the parties agree to a known event, even if the exact date is uncertain. However, the Hanafi school insists on a precise calendar date to avoid jahalah.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; the Hanafi position is more cautious to prevent disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١٧) والبيع الى النيروز والمهرجان وصوم النصارى وفطر اليهود اذا لم يكن البائع والمشترى يعرفانه فالبيع فاسد. تشریح یوں کہا کہ میں نیروز کے دن بیع کرتا ہوں ہمشمسی سال کے پہلے دن کو نیروز کہتے ہیں۔ اور پارسیوں کے عید کے دن کو مہر جان کہتے ہیں ۔ اب ان دنوں میں بیج کیا اور بائع اور مشتری کو یہ معلوم نہیں ہے کہ نیروز کس دن ہے اور مہر جان کس دن ہے تو وقت مجہول ہو گیا اس لئے بیع فاسد ہوگی۔ حدیث میں گزر چکا ہے کہ بیچ میں اجل معلوم ہونا چاہئے ۔ عن ابن عباس قال قدم النبي الله المدينة وهم يسلفون في الثمار السنتين والثلاث فقال اسلفوا في الثمار في كيل معلوم الى اجل معلوم (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب السلم الی اجل معلوم ص ٣٠٠ نمبر ٢٢٥٣ ر مسلم شریف، باب السلم ص ١٣١ نمبر ١٦٠٤) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیچ میں اجل معلوم ہو تب بیع جائز ہوگی۔ ور نه مشتری جلدی مانگے گا اور بائع مبیع دیر کر کے دے گا۔ اس لئے بیع فاسد ہوگی۔
(17) And selling to Nowruz, Mihrajan, the fast of Christians, or the breaking of the fast of Jews, if the seller and buyer do not know them, the sale is void. Explanation: He said 'I sell on the day of Nowruz' — Nowruz is the first day of the solar year, Mihrajan is the festival of the Zoroastrians. If they do not know when these occur, the time is unknown, so the sale is void. The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas states that the Prophet allowed salam with a known measure and known term. Hence the time in a sale must be known; otherwise, the sale is void.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage deals with a sale where the time of delivery or payment is set to an indeterminate future date, such as a festival whose date is not commonly known. The Hanafi ruling is that such a sale is fasid (void) because the term (ajal) is unknown, leading to uncertainty (jahalah) that can cause disputes. The proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas regarding salam: the Prophet instructed that salam must specify a known measure and a known term. This principle applies to all deferred contracts. The text gives examples: Nowruz (Persian New Year), Mihrajan (Zoroastrian festival), Christian fasting (Lent or Easter), and Jewish breaking of fast (Yom Kippur or similar) — if these dates are not known to the parties, the contract is invalid. The reasoning is that ignorance of the time leads to potential conflict.

Key Terms
النيروز (al-nayruz): The Persian New Year, a solar festival whose date varies.
المهرجان (al-mihrajan): A Zoroastrian festival; here used as an example of an unknown date.
أجل معلوم (ajal ma'lum): A fixed and known term or deadline for delivery or payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A sale with an unknown future term (ajal majhul) is fasid because it leads to gharar; the term must be known to both parties.

Sale with Conditional Tailoring and Unknown Terms
Ruling and proof on conditional services and uncertain terms in sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional tailoring in a sale, identify the hadith proof, and apply the distinction between fasid and batil in deferred sales with uncertain terms.

Core Idea
A sale combined with a conditional service or an unknown term is fasid, but custom or cancelling the term may cure it.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling from Kitab al-Buyu'. The passage addresses three interrelated issues: (1) buying cloth with the condition that the seller also tailors it, (2) deferring payment to a festival date unknown to the parties, and (3) deferring to an uncertain agricultural event. All three are ruled fasid due to gharar (uncertainty). The lesson unpacks the proof from hadith and the legal consequences of a fasid sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional sale and its ruling
Read the first sentence: buying cloth on condition that the seller cuts and sews it. The ruling is 'fasid' (voidable).
The condition creates a combination of sale and hire (ijarah).
2
Understand the dalil and its application
The hadith 'two sales in one' is cited. Discuss how including an ijarah element in the sale violates this prohibition.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), hence the ruling is not fard/haram but fasid.
3
Distinguish unknown terms in deferred sales
The passage lists deferrals to Nawroz, Mihrajan, Christian fast, Jewish feast – if unknown to parties, the sale is fasid due to ajal majhul.
Also deferrals to harvest, threshing, etc. are not permissible unless the term is cancelled before the event.
4
Analyze the legal effect of a fasid sale
After possession with seller's permission, ownership transfers and price becomes wajib, but both parties have rescission rights. Resale by buyer is valid.
This distinguishes fasid from batil: fasid can become effective if defects are cured.
5
Note the role of custom ('urf)
Custom may override the default ruling: if tailoring is customary, the sale becomes valid. This is an application of istihsan.
The mufta bihi position accepts custom as a determinant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشترى ثوبا على ان يقطعه البائع ويخيطه قميصا او قباء او نعلا على ان يحذوها او يشركها فالبيع فاسد. والبيع الى النيروز والمهرجان وصوم النصارى وفطر اليهود اذا لم يعرف المتبايعان ذلك فاسد. ولا يجوز البيع الى الحصاد والدياس والقطاف وقدوم الحاج فان تراضيا باسقاط الاجل قبل ان يأخذ الناس في الحصاد والدياس وقبل قدوم الحاج جاز البيع. اذا قبض المشترى المبيع بيعة فاسدة بامر البائع وكان العوضان مالين في العقد ملك المبيع ووجبت عليه قيمته ولكل واحد منهما فسخ البيع فان باع المشترى المبيع جاز بيعه.
If someone buys a cloth on condition that the seller cuts it and sews it into a shirt or a cloak, or buys sandals on condition that he shapes them or straps them, then the sale is void. The sale to Nawroz, Mihrajan, the fast of the Christians, and the breaking of the fast of the Jews, if the two transacting parties do not know that, is void. And the sale to harvest, threshing, fruit-cutting, and the arrival of the Hajj is not permissible. If they mutually agree to drop the term before people begin harvesting and threshing and before the arrival of the Hajj, the sale becomes permissible. If the buyer takes possession of the sold item in a void sale by the command of the seller, and the two countervalues in the contract are properties, the buyer becomes owner of the sold item and its price becomes obligatory upon him. Each of them has the right to rescind the sale. If the buyer resells the sold item, his sale is valid.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage bundles several rulings from Kitab al-Buyu'. The first ruling concerns a sale conditioned on the seller providing additional services like cutting and sewing. Such a condition benefits the buyer and introduces an element of hire (ijarah) into the sale, making it fasid. The Hanafi school cites the hadith prohibiting 'two sales in one transaction.' However, if local custom accepts such transactions, the sale becomes valid. The second ruling deals with deferring payment to festival days unknown to the parties, which makes the sale fasid due to ignorance of the term. The third ruling similarly prohibits deferment to uncertain agricultural events, but if the parties cancel the term before the event, the sale is valid. The fourth ruling explains the legal effect of a fasid sale: if possession is taken with the seller's permission, ownership and price become binding, but each party retains the right to rescind. Subsequent resale by the buyer is valid.

Key Terms
بيع فاسد (bay' fasid): A sale that is invalid due to a defect in its conditions or subject matter, but can become valid if the defect is removed.
اجل مجهول (ajal majhul): A term or deadline that is unknown, leading to uncertainty (gharar) and invalidating the sale.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows deviation from a ruling in favor of a more suitable outcome, often based on custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone buys cloth on condition that the seller also sews it into a shirt, the sale is:
A) Valid (sahih)
B) Void (batil)
C) Voidable (fasid)
D) Recommended (mandub)

Key Takeaway
A sale conditioned on an additional service is fasid by default, but custom can make it valid; fasid sales transfer ownership after possession but remain rescindable.

Ruling on Sale with an Unknown Term (Ajal Majhul)
States the ruling that sale with an unspecified term is fasid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale with an unspecified term, identify the reason for its defectiveness, and apply the condition that allows the sale to become valid.

Core Idea
A sale with an unknown future term is fasid; only if the term is dropped before it begins does the sale become valid.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on sales where the payment or delivery is deferred to an uncertain date, such as 'until harvest' or 'until the pilgrims arrive.' The source passage from the matn gives the ruling and a proof from Ibn Abbas. We will unpack why such a term renders the sale fasid (defective) and how parties can rectify it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
The passage states that selling with a term like 'until harvest' or 'until the pilgrim's arrival' is not permissible. The act is a sale with a deferred payment or delivery, and the ruling is fasid (defective).
The term 'fasid' means the contract is valid in essence but has a defect that can be remedied.
2
Understand the defect and its removal
The defect is the unknown term (ajal majhul). The passage says that if the parties mutually agree to drop the term before the event occurs, the sale becomes valid. This shows that the defect is in the condition, not the contract's substance.
The condition must be dropped before the unspecified event begins, e.g., before harvest starts.
3
Examine the proof from Hadith
Ibn Abbas narrates that there is no salaf (advance sale) for unspecified terms like 'until the stipend, until harvest, until threshing.' This hadith (reported in Sunan al-Bayhaqi) is used as evidence that the term must be known for a deferred sale to be valid.
The hadith is ahad and zanni in both transmission and meaning, but it is accepted by the Hanafi school in this context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اليهود اذا لم يعرف المتبايعان ذلك فاسد ولا يجوز البيع الى الحصاد والدياس والقطاف وقدوم الحاج فان تراضيا باسقاط الاجل قبل ان يأخذ الناس في الحصاد والدياس وقبل قدوم الحاج جاز البيع. عن ابن عباس قال لا سلف الي العطاء ولا الى الحصاد ولا الى الاندر.
A sale to Jews when the two parties do not know that [the time] is invalid. And it is not permissible to sell until harvest, threshing, fruit-picking, and the arrival of the pilgrim. But if they mutually agree to drop the term before the people start harvesting, threshing, and before the pilgrim arrives, the sale is valid. Ibn Abbas said: There is no salaf (advance sale) until the stipend, nor until harvest, nor until threshing.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage lays out the ruling on sales where the future term (ajal) is unspecified. The Hanafi school considers a sale fasid (defective) if the term is ambiguous, such as 'until harvest' or 'until the pilgrims come,' because the exact date is unknown. The example of selling to Jews refers to using their festivals as terms—these are also unknown to the general public. The key principle is that jahalah (ignorance) in the term renders the sale defective. However, if the parties drop the condition before the term begins, the sale becomes valid because the defect is removed before it takes effect. The hadith from Ibn Abbas forbids salaf (advance payment sale) with such unknown terms, reinforcing the ruling.

Key Terms
اجل مجهول (ajal majhul): A future term that is not specified or known, e.g., 'until harvest'.
الحصاد (al-hasad): The harvest of crops; an uncertain time reference.
الدياس (al-diyas): Threshing of grains; another uncertain time reference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a sale where the payment is deferred 'until the pilgrims arrive'?
A) It is valid because the term is a known event.
B) It is fasid (defective) because the exact date is unknown.
C) It is batil (void) because it involves uncertainty.
D) It is mubah (permissible) if both parties agree.

Key Takeaway
A sale with an unspecified future term is fasid due to jahalah; it can become valid if the term is dropped before it begins.

Ownership Transfer in a Defective Sale (Bay' Fasid)
States the Hanafi ruling on possession in a defective sale with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for ownership transfer via possession in a fasid sale and explain the legal effect using the Hanafi classification.

Core Idea
In a defective sale, possession with seller's permission transfers ownership, but the buyer owes market value.

This lesson explores a distinctive aspect of Hanafi fiqh: although a sale may be defective (fasid) due to a missing condition, it can still transfer ownership through possession. We will examine the ruling, the required conditions, and the underlying proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ‘possession (qabd) in a defective sale (bay‘ fasid)’. The ruling is that the buyer becomes owner of the item and must pay its market value, provided three conditions are met.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes fasid from batil; fasid can produce certain effects.
2
Locate the dalil
The source cites a hadith from Sunan Abu Dawud (no. 3332) about a man who bought a goat without the seller’s permission. The Prophet (ﷺ) instructed to feed the goat to prisoners, indicating ownership had transferred.
The hadith is ahad (single narration) with zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet (ﷺ) did not order the buyer to return the goat; instead, he allowed it to be consumed. This implies that the buyer owned the goat despite the defective sale (lack of owner’s permission).
The imperative ‘aṭ‘im’ (feed) is taken as a sign of ownership.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi‘i holds that a fasid sale is essentially batil (void) and cannot transfer ownership even after possession; the item must be returned to the seller.
This disagreement stems from a different classification of defective contracts.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the explicit hadith and the principle that fasid is valid in substance (arkan present) but defective in a condition. Thus, possession rectifies the defect to the extent of ownership.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اذا قبض المشترى المبيع في البيع الفاسد بامر البائع وفى العقد عوضان كل واحد منهما مال ملک المبيع ولزمته قيمته ولكل واحد من المتعاقدين فسخه فان باعه المشترى نفذ بيعه. عن رجل من الانصار قال خرجنا مع رسول الله في جنازة ... فارسلت الى امرأته فارسلت إلى بها فقال رسول الله اطعميه الاساری.
When the buyer takes possession of the sold item in a defective sale by the command of the seller, and in the contract both countervalues are property, he becomes owner of the sold item, and its market value becomes due upon him; either of the two contractors may rescind it; then if the buyer sells it, his sale is valid. A man from the Ansar said: We went out with the Messenger of God in a funeral... and he sent to his wife, and she sent it to him, so the Messenger of God said: 'Feed it to the prisoners.'
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage explains the legal effects of possession (qabd) in a defective sale (bay' fasid). According to the Hanafi madhhab, a fasid sale is one that lacks a condition of validity but not a pillar; thus the substance of the contract is sound. If the buyer takes possession with the seller's permission, and both the sold item and the price are property (i.e., not a free person or impure substance), then the buyer becomes the owner of the item. However, he must pay the market value (qimah) rather than the agreed price. Both parties have the right to rescind (faskh) the contract. If the buyer resells the item, the second sale is valid because the buyer had valid ownership. The hadith about the goat purchased without the owner's permission illustrates this: the buyer owned it after possession but the Prophet avoided eating it due to the defect. The ruling encourages resolution without dispute.

Key Terms
البيع الفاسد (al-bay' al-fasid): A contract that is valid in substance but defective in a condition (e.g., unknown term or extra benefit).
قبض (qabd): Taking physical possession of the sold item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a defective sale (bay' fasid), when does the buyer become owner of the purchased item?
A) At the contract of sale, regardless of possession.
B) Only if he takes possession with the seller's permission, and both items are property.
C) Only if he pays the full agreed price.
D) He never becomes owner; the sale is void.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, possession in a fasid sale with the seller's permission and both items being property transfers ownership, making subsequent transactions valid.

Combining Disparate Items in a Sale: The Ruling of Batil
Ruling on combining impermissible items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining a permissible and impermissible item in a single sale, and explain why the entire contract becomes batil.

Core Idea
Including a non-commodity or impure item in a sale voids the entire contract completely.

This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri presents a concise ruling about combining incompatible items in one sale. The Hanafi school holds that a sale must involve legally valid objects; if even one item is non-sellable, the contract is void ab initio. This teaching examines the principle and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the combined items
Recognize the two cases given: (1) free person + slave, (2) slaughtered goat + dead goat. Note that in each case, one item is legally sellable (slave, slaughtered goat) and the other is not (free person, dead goat).
The free person (hurr) is not a commodity; the dead goat (maytah) is najis and cannot be sold.
2
Determine the legal status of each item
In Hanafi fiqh, a free person is not mal (wealth) and cannot be the subject of a sale. A dead goat is najis and lacks the condition of purity (tahara) for a valid sale. Slaves and slaughtered goats are valid objects of sale.
The invalidity arises from the inherent nature of the item, not from a defect in the contract.
3
Apply the ruling: batil
Because the contract includes an item that is not a valid mabi', the entire sale becomes batil. The Hanafi school does not allow splitting a single contract; the presence of one invalid component nullifies the whole.
Compare to fasid: batil cannot be rectified; the contract is void from the start.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The unity of the contract means that the consideration (price) is in exchange for all items together. If any item is invalid, the consideration is not properly specified, leading to gharar (uncertainty) and batil.
This principle also applies when combining permissible and impermissible items in other contracts like lease or gift.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی نے بیچ میں آزاد اور غلام کو جمع کیا یا ذبح شدہ بکری اور مردہ بکری کو جمع کیا تو بیع دونوں میں باطل ہے.
If someone combined in a sale a free person and a slave, or a slaughtered goat and a dead goat, then the sale in both is void.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This short ruling addresses a specific case of combining legally incompatible items in a single contract. In Hanafi fiqh, a free person (hurr) is not a valid object of sale (mabi'), so including him renders the contract batil (void). Similarly, a dead goat (maytah) is najis and not permissible to sell, while a slaughtered goat (dhabihah) is halal and sellable. When both are combined in one sale, the entire contract becomes batil because the contract cannot be partially valid. This is stricter than a fasid sale; here the contract is void ab initio. The ruling emphasizes that the presence of any non-commodity (like a free person) or impure item (like a dead animal) invalidates the entire transaction.

Key Terms
باطل (batil): A contract that is void in substance and produces no legal effects.
جمع (jama'a): Combining two items in one contract of sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a seller combines the sale of a permissible slaughtered goat and an impermissible dead goat in one contract?
A) The sale of the slaughtered goat is valid, the dead goat is void.
B) The entire sale is void (batil).
C) The sale is fasid and can be corrected by removing the dead goat.
D) The buyer has the choice to accept or reject.

Key Takeaway
Combining a legally valid item with an invalid one in a single sale makes the entire contract void (batil) in Hanafi law.

Conditions for Ownership in a Fasid Sale
Ruling with proof on ownership conditions in a fasid sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for ownership transfer in a fasid sale according to the Hanafi school and explain the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
In a fasid sale, ownership transfers only after possession with consent, provided both items are property.

In Hanafi fiqh, a fasid (voidable) sale is valid in its core but defective due to an external condition. This lesson examines the three conditions that must be met for the buyer to become owner of the sold item. We will also study the hadith proof that the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed the buyer to feed the goat to prisoners, establishing ownership transfer despite the defect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
In a fasid sale, ownership transfers if three conditions are met: (1) buyer takes possession, (2) with seller's consent, (3) both items are property. Note that each party initially has the right to rescind.
2
Understand the nature of the defect
The defect in a fasid sale is not in the core contract (asl al-aqd) but in an external condition, such as unknown term or prohibited benefit. If a dispute arises, the sale is invalidated; but if possession occurs without dispute, ownership transfers.
3
Trace the hadith proof
The author cites a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud about a goat sold without the owner's permission. The Prophet ordered the buyer to feed the goat to prisoners, indicating ownership after possession, though he refrained himself due to disapproval.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah, but sufficient for this ruling.
4
Note the inter-madhhab difference
Imam Shafi'i holds that possession does not transfer ownership in a fasid sale; the buyer must return the item. The Hanafi school relies on the hadith as evidence.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions are valid in their own usul.
5
Summarize the practical takeaway
In a fasid sale with the three conditions met, the buyer becomes owner and must pay the market value. The sale remains makruh (disapproved) but not batil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيوع في البيع الفاسد بامر البائع وفى العقد عوضان كل واحد منهما مال ملک المبيع ولزمته قيمته ولكل واحد من المتعاقدين فسخه فان باعه المشترى نفذ بيعه [ ٩٠١](٢٠) ومن تین شرطیں پائی جائیں تو بیع فاسد میں مشتری مبیع کا مالک بنتا ہے (۱) مشتری نے مبیع پر قبضہ کیا ہو (۲) بائع کی رضامندی سے قبضہ کیا۔ ہو (۳) مبیع اور شمن دونوں ہی مال ہوں۔ یہ تینوں شرطیں پائی جائیں تو مشتری مبیع کا مالک بنتا ہے۔ اور اس پر مبیع کی بازاری قیمت لازم ہوگی (1) بیع فاسد میں صلب عقد اور اصل عقد میں خامی نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ دونوں جانب مال ہیں۔ اس لئے مالک ہو جائیں گے۔ یہاں خامی تو شرط میں ہے کہ کہیں مدت مجہول ہے۔ کسی بیچ میں بائع کا فائدہ تو کسی بیچ میں مشتری کا فائدہ ہے۔ اور کسی بیچ میں مبیع بائع کی ملکیت سے علیحدہ نہیں ہے جس کی وجہ سے بیع فاسد کی گئی ہے۔ کیونکہ کسی میں دھوکہ ہے اور کہیں جھگڑا ہونے کا خطرہ ہے۔ اس کی پیش بندی کی وجہ سے بیع فاسد کی گئی۔ لیکن اگر جھگڑا نہیں ہوا اور آخر مشتری نے قبضہ کر ہی لیا تو آخریع جائز قرار دیدی جائے گی (۲) اس کا ثبوت حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ جنازے سے واپس آرہے تھے۔ ایک عورت نے دعوت کی ۔ انہوں نے بکری خریدنے کے لئے آدمی بھیجا لیکن نہیں ملی ۔ آخر ایک عورت نے اپنے شوہر کی بکری بغیر اس کی اجازت کے بیچ دی۔ اور دعوت کرنے والی نے ذبح کر کے حضور کو کھلانے کے لئے پیش کی ۔ آپ کو وحی کے ذریعہ معلوم ہوا کہ اس بکری کے خریدنے میں خامی ہے۔ عورت کو پوچھنے پر معلوم ہوا مالک کی اجازت کے بغیر بکری دی گئی ہے۔ اور بیع فاسد ہے۔ لیکن آپ نے یہ نہیں فرمایا کہ عورت کی ملکیت نہیں ہوئی بلکہ یوں فرمایا کہ یہ کھانا قیدیوں کو کھلا دو۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ قبضہ کے بعد عورت کی ملکیت تو ہو گئی اس لئے قیدیوں کو کھلا دو۔ لیکن اس میں کراہیت ضرور ہے اس لئے خود آپ نے نوش نہیں فرمایا۔ عن رجل من الانصار قال خرجنا مع رسول الله الله الله في جنازة ... فارسلت الى امرأته فارسلت إلى بها فقال رسول الله الله اطعميه الاساری (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی اجتناب الشبہات ص ۱۶ انمبر ۳۳۳۲) اس حدیث میں اشارہ ہے کہ بیع فاسد میں قبضہ کے بعد مشتری مبیع کا مالک بن جائے گا۔
Book of Sales. Regarding the fasid sale by the buyer's command, and in the contract there are two compensations, each of which is property, ownership of the sold item is transferred and its value becomes obligatory, and each of the two contracting parties has the right to rescind it. If the buyer sells it, his sale is effective. [901](20) When three conditions are found, in a fasid sale the buyer becomes the owner of the sold item: (1) the buyer has taken possession of the sold item, (2) possession was taken with the seller's consent, (3) both the sold item and the price are property. If these three conditions are found, the buyer becomes the owner of the sold item and the market price of the sold item becomes incumbent upon him. (1) In a fasid sale, there is no defect in the core contract and the original contract, because both sides are property. Therefore, they will become owners. The defect here is in the condition, such as where the term is unknown, in some transactions the seller has a benefit, in some the buyer has a benefit, and in some the sold item is not separated from the seller's ownership, due to which the fasid sale was made. Because in some there is deception and in some there is a risk of dispute. Due to precaution, the fasid sale was made. But if no dispute occurred and eventually the buyer took possession, then the transaction will be considered valid. (2) Its proof is in the hadith: He (peace be upon him) was returning from a funeral. A woman invited him. He sent a man to buy a goat but it was not available. Finally, a woman sold her husband's goat without his permission. The inviter slaughtered it and presented it to the Prophet (peace be upon him) to eat. He was informed through revelation that there was a defect in the purchase of this goat. When he asked the woman, it became known that the goat was given without the owner's permission and the sale was fasid. But he did not say that the woman had not become owner; rather he said, 'Feed this food to the prisoners.' This meant that after possession, the woman's ownership had occurred, so feed it to the prisoners. But there was certainly disapproval in it, so he himself did not partake. From a man of the Ansar, he said: We went out with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for a funeral... He sent to his wife and she sent it to me. Then the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Feed it to the prisoners.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on avoiding doubtful matters, p. 16, no. 3332). This hadith indicates that in a fasid sale, after possession, the buyer becomes the owner of the sold item.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the conditions for ownership transfer in a fasid (voidable) sale according to the Hanafi school. The author first states the general rule: in a fasid sale, each party has the right to rescind, but if the conditions are met, the buyer becomes owner of the sold item and must pay its market value. The three conditions are: (1) the buyer must have taken physical possession (qabd), (2) that possession must be with the seller's consent, and (3) both the sold item and the price must be property (mal) in the legal sense. The author explains that in a fasid sale, the defect is not in the core contract (asl al-aqd) but in a condition or description, such as unknown term or undue benefit. If a dispute arises, the sale is invalidated; but if possession occurs without dispute, the sale becomes valid retroactively. The proof is a hadith from Abu Dawud about a sale without the husband's permission: the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the buyer to feed the goat to prisoners, indicating ownership was established after possession, though the sale was disapproved. This passage is typical of Hanafi fiqh methodology: stating the ruling with conditions, explaining the rationale, and providing a hadith proof.

Key Terms
البيع الفاسد (al-bay' al-fasid): A sale that is valid in its essence (core contract) but defective due to a condition or description (e.g., unknown term, prohibited benefit).
القبض (al-qabd): Physical possession or taking control of the sold item with the seller's consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid sale, what is the effect if the buyer takes possession with the seller's consent?
A) The buyer becomes owner and must pay the market price.
B) The buyer must return the item immediately.
C) The sale is void and no ownership transfers.
D) The buyer becomes owner only if the seller explicitly confirms.

Key Takeaway
In a fasid sale, ownership transfers after possession with consent, but the sale remains makruh (disapproved) and the buyer must pay the market price.

Effect of Buyer's Resale in Fasid Sale
Ruling on validity of buyer's resale in fasid sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a buyer's resale of an item acquired through a fasid sale and explain the reasoning based on the distinction between defect in core vs. condition and the precedence of haqq al-'abd.

Core Idea
A buyer's resale in a fasid sale is valid because the defect is external and the third party's right overrides the Shariah's minor right.

This passage explains a key Hanafi distinction: a fasid (voidable) sale is not completely without effect. If the buyer takes possession and then resells to a third party, that second sale is valid and binding. The reasoning hinges on two principles: the defect in the first sale was only in a condition, not the core contract, and the right of the person (haqq al-'abd) takes precedence over a minor right of the Shariah. This ruling highlights the practical flexibility of Hanafi fiqh in sales transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the buyer's resale of an item acquired in a fasid sale. The ruling: the second sale is valid (nāfidh) and effective.
The ruling applies after the buyer has taken possession.
2
Understand the distinction between fasid and batil
Fasid: defect in a condition/description, not the core contract. Batil: defect in the core itself (e.g., item not owned). In fasid, ownership can transfer; in batil, it cannot.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the principle of haqq al-'abd vs. haqq Allah
The defect in the first sale involved a Shariah right (haqq Allah). The third party's ownership in the second sale is a person's right (haqq al-'abd). The latter prevails, making the second sale valid.
This principle is used to resolve conflicts between rights.
4
Contrast with batil sale
If the first sale were batil (defect in core), no ownership transfers, so any subsequent sale would be void regardless of possession.
This reinforces why the condition/core distinction matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بیع فاسد میں مشتری نے قبضہ کی ہوئی مبیع کو دوسرے کے ہاتھ میں بیچ دیا تو دوسری بیع نافذ ہو گئی ۔ کیونکہ پہلی بیچ کے اصل عقد میں خامی نہیں تھی۔ صرف اس کے وصف اور شرط میں خامی تھی اور وہ بھی جھگڑا اٹھے بغیر نمٹ گئی تو پہلی بیع بھی نافذ ہوگئی (۲) پہلی بیع کی خامی میں شریعت کا حق تھا اور دوسری بیع میں بندے کا حق ہے۔ اور بندے کا حق مقدم ہے اس لئے بندے کے حق کی وجہ سے شریعت کا چھوٹا موٹا حق ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے مشتری کی بیع نافذ ہو جائے گی۔ اور صلب عقد اور اصل عقد میں خامی ہو تو بیع باطل ہوگی۔ اس صورت میں بائع اور مشتری کی رضامندی کے باوجود بھی مشتری بیع کا مالک نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ بیچ ہوئی ہی نہیں۔
In a fasid sale, if the buyer sells the possessed item to another person, the second sale is effective. Because the first sale's core contract had no defect; only its description and condition had a defect, and that too was settled without dispute, so the first sale also became effective. (2) In the defect of the first sale, there was a right of the Shariah, and in the second sale, there is a right of the servant. And the right of the servant takes precedence, so due to the right of the servant, the minor right of the Shariah falls away. Therefore, the buyer's sale is effective. And if there is a defect in the core contract and original contract, then the sale is batil (void). In that case, despite the consent of the seller and buyer, the buyer will not become the owner of the sold item. Rather, the sale never occurred.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the validity of a resale by the buyer in a fasid (voidable) sale. The author explains that after the buyer takes possession, if he sells the item to a third party, that second sale is valid and effective. The reasoning is that the defect in the original fasid sale was only in an external condition or description, not in the core contract (asl al-aqd). Since the first sale was resolved without dispute, it becomes effective, and the buyer gained ownership. The second sale involves the right of a person (the third-party buyer), which takes precedence over a minor right of the Shariah (the defect in the first sale). Therefore, the second sale is valid and overrides the imperfection of the first. By contrast, if the defect is in the core contract itself (e.g., selling what does not exist), the sale is batil (void) and no ownership transfers, even if the buyer takes possession and resells; the resale would be void as well. This ruling highlights the Hanafi distinction between fasid and batil, and the principle that the right of a person (haqq al-'abd) can outweigh a lesser right of the Shariah (haqq al-shar').

Key Terms
صلب العقد (sulb al-'aqd): The core or essence of the contract, as opposed to external conditions or descriptions.
حق العبد (haqq al-'abd): The right of a human being (e.g., ownership, compensation), as opposed to the right of Allah (haqq Allah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the first sale's defect was only in a condition, and the third party's right overrides the Shariah's minor right.
B) Because the buyer had the seller's permission.
C) Because the first sale was already valid from the start.
D) Because the buyer did not take possession.

Key Takeaway
A buyer's resale in a fasid sale is valid because the defect is in a condition, not the core, and the rights of the third party take precedence over the Shariah's minor right.
