Sale Combining Permissible and Impermissible Items
Ruling on combining a free person and a slave, or a slaughtered and dead goat in one sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a valid and invalid item are combined in one sale contract, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding separate pricing.

Core Idea
Combining a non-salable item with a salable one in one contract voids the entire sale, unless prices are separately stated (Sahibayn's view).

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling on combining lawful and unlawful items in a single sale. The core principle is that a contract cannot simultaneously effect a valid and invalid transaction; the defect spreads to the whole. However, the two disciples of Abu Hanifa introduced a nuance based on separate pricing. Understanding this dispute sharpens your appreciation of how Hanafi jurists balance contractual unity with fairness in exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is combining two items in one sale: one valid (slave/slaughtered goat) and one invalid (free person/dead goat). The ruling: the entire sale is batil.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
Two reasons: (a) the invalid item is not property, so its sale is void; (b) the contract is one, so the defect spreads; (c) ignorance (jahl) arises regarding the price allocation for the valid item.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds the sale is batil even if prices are separate. The Sahibayn say if prices are stated separately, the valid item's sale is valid.
4
Compare the proofs
Abu Hanifa emphasizes the unity of the contract; the Sahibayn emphasize removal of jahl.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's for caution, but the Sahibayn's view is applied when needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۹۰۱] (۲۰) کسی نے بیچ میں آزاد اور غلام کو جمع کیا یا ذبح شدہ بکری اور مردہ بکری کو جمع کیا تو بیع دونوں میں باطل ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) فرمایا ہم حضور کے ساتھ ایک جنازے میں لکھے.. میں نے اس کی بیوی بل پاس خبر بھیجی کہ بکری دے دو تو انہوں نے بکری میرے پاس بھیج دی۔ پس آپ نے فرمایا یہ کھانا قیدیوں کو کھلا دو۔
آزاد بیع ہی نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح مردہ بکری مبیع ہی نہیں ہے اس لئے ان کی بیع ہی نہیں ہوئی۔ اور عقد ایک ہے اس لئے اس کا اثر دوسری مبیع یعنی غلام اور ذبح شدہ بکری پر بھی پڑے گا اور ان کی بیع بھی نہیں ہوگی (۲) آزاد اور مردہ بکری کی بیع نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے غلام اور ذبح شدہ بکری کی قیمت میں جہالت آگئی اس لئے غلام اور ذبح شدہ بکری کی بیع بھی نہیں ہوگی۔
اصول یہاں یہ اصول ہے کہ آزاد اور مردہ بکری کی بیع ہوئی ہی نہیں اس لئے ان کے اثر سے غلام اور ذبح شدہ بکری کی بیج بھی فاسد ہوگی۔ فائده صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ غلام کی قیمت الگ بیان کی ہو اور آزاد کی قیمت الگ بیان کی ہو تو غلام کی بیچ ہو جائے گی چاہے دونوں ایک عقد میں بکے ہوں۔
کیونکہ دونوں کی قیمت الگ الگ ہونے کی وجہ سے آزاد کی بیع نہیں ہوئی تو غلام کی قیمت میں جہالت نہیں رہی اس لئے غلام کی بیع فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔ اسی طرح ذبح شدہ بکری کی کی قیمت الگ بیان کی گئی ہو تو مردہ بکری کی بیع نہیں ہوئی تب بھی ذبح شدہ بکری کی قیمت میں جہالت نہیں رہی اس لئے ذبح شدہ بکری کی بیچ ہا جائے گی۔ ت ذكية : ذبح کی ہوئی۔
[901](20) If someone combines in a sale a free person and a slave, or a slaughtered goat and a dead goat, the sale is void in both. Footnote (a): He said: We were with the Prophet (peace be upon him) in a funeral... I sent to his wife to give the goat, and she sent the goat to me. Then the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Feed this food to the prisoners.'
A free person is not salable; similarly, a dead goat is not salable, so their sale did not occur. And since the contract is one, its effect will fall on the other sold item, i.e., the slave and the slaughtered goat, so their sale will also not occur. (2) Because of the non-sale of the free person and dead goat, ignorance (jahl) arose regarding the price of the slave and slaughtered goat, so their sale also does not occur. 
The principle here is that since the free person and dead goat were not sold, due to their effect, the sale of the slave and slaughtered goat is also fasid. Benefit: The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: If the price of the slave is stated separately and the price of the free person is stated separately, then the sale of the slave will be valid even if both were sold in one contract. Because due to the separate prices, the free person's sale did not occur, so there is no ignorance in the slave's price, and thus the slave's sale is not fasid. Similarly, if the price of the slaughtered goat is stated separately, then the dead goat's sale did not occur, so there is no ignorance in the slaughtered goat's price, and thus the slaughtered goat's sale will be valid. T. dhakiyya: slaughtered.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the effect of combining a lawful and an unlawful item in a single sale contract. According to the Hanafi school, if one combines a free person (which is not salable property) with a slave, or a slaughtered (halal) goat with a dead (carrion) goat, the entire sale is void (batil). The reason is that the free person and dead goat are not valid subjects of sale, so their inclusion invalidates the contract. Because the contract is indivisible, the defect extends to the other item, and also ignorance (jahl) arises regarding the allocation of the price, which invalidates the sale of the valid item. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) have an exception: if the price of each item is separately stated, then the sale of the valid item (slave or slaughtered goat) is valid, while the sale of the invalid item is void. In that case, there is no ignorance regarding the price of the valid item. This is an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa holds that the entire sale is void regardless of separate pricing, while the Sahibayn allow validity if prices are separated. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the school is often that of Abu Hanifa for caution, but the Sahibayn's view is also considered. The footnote (a) refers to the earlier hadith, indicating that the Prophet did not eat the goat because it was sold without permission, but ordered it to be fed to prisoners, showing ownership after possession.

Key Terms
البيع الباطل (al-bay' al-batil): A sale that is void ab initio due to a defect in the core contract (e.g., selling a free person or carrion).
الجهالة (al-jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding the price or subject matter that invalidates a sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when is the sale of a slave valid if combined with a free person in one contract?
A) The sale of the slave is valid if the buyer and seller agree.
B) The sale of the slave is valid only if its price is stated separately from the free person.
C) The sale of the slave is always valid regardless of pricing.
D) The sale of the slave is never valid in such a combination.

Key Takeaway
Combining a non-salable item with a salable one in one contract makes the entire sale batil, unless the prices are stated separately (Sahibayn's view).

Partial Validity When Combining a Slave and a Mudabbir in Sale
Ruling with proof on partial validity of sale when combining a regular slave with a mudabbir or another’s slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale combining two items when one is non-salable, and apply the principle of partial validity using the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Sale of a regular slave stands even if combined with a non-salable item.

In Hanafi fiqh, if a person sells a regular slave together with a mudabbir (a slave promised freedom after the master's death) or with another person's slave without permission, the contract is not entirely void. The sale of the regular slave is valid and the buyer pays its proportionate price. This lesson explores the ruling, its proof from the Sunnah, and the intra-madhhab dispute on the salability of a mudabbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is selling a regular slave (ghulam) together with a mudabbir or another's slave. The ruling is that the sale of the regular slave is valid (sahih) for its share of the price.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari where the Prophet (peace be upon him) sold a mudabbir. This proves mudabbir is property and salable in principle.
Hadith reference: Bukhari, Book of Sales, chapter on sale of mudabbir.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The explicit action of the Prophet (selling a mudabbir) establishes that a mudabbir is a valid subject of sale. Thus, when combined with a regular slave, the contract is not void because the mudabbir is salable in itself; but due to the legal impediment (the promise of freedom), its sale fails individually, leaving the regular slave's sale intact.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, Abu Hanifa held that a mudabbir is not salable, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held it is salable. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the Sahibayn, following the hadith evidence.
Inter-madhhab: Shafi'i also requires consent for sale of mudabbir.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The Sahibayn's position is preferred due to the explicit hadith and its stronger dalalah. The ruling is that the regular slave's sale is valid and the buyer pays its share.
The principle extends to any sale where one item in a bundle cannot be sold for a reason: the valid item's sale stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٩٠٢) (۲۱) کسی نے غلام اور مدبر کوجمع کیا یا اپنے غلا اور غیر کے غلام کو بچ میں جمع کیا تو غلام میں ہی صحیح ہوئی اس کی قیمت کے حصے کے ساتھ۔
انا غلام اور مدبر غلام دونوں کو ایک بیچ میں جمع کر دیا۔ یا اپنے غلام کو اور دوسرے کے غلام کو بغیر اس کی اجازت کے ایک بیع میں جمع کر دیا تو مدبر کی بیچ تو نہیں ہوگی لیکن خالص غلام کی بیچ ہو جائے گی۔ اور جو قیمت اس کے حصے کی ہوگی وہ لازم ہوگی۔ مثلا دو ہزار کے غلام اور مدبر تھے تو خالص غلام کی قیمت ایک ہزار رہ گئی تو ایک ہزار لازم ہوں گے۔ اسی طرح دوسرے کا غلام اس کی اجازت کے بغیر بیج میں داخل نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن اپنے غلام کی بیچ ہو جائے گی۔ اور جو اس کے حصے کی قیمت ہے وہ مشتری پر لازم ہوگی۔ مد بر کسی نہ کسی امام کے نزدیک غلام کی طرح بکنے کے قابل ہے اس لئے وہ مال ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن جابر قال باع النبی اے المدبر (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب بیع المد بر ص ۲۹۷ نمبر ۲۲۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مر بر غلام بکنے کے قابل ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو خالص غلام کے ساتھ ملایا تو بیع ہو گئی۔ اب بعد میں مدبر کی بیع نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی قیمت الگ ہوگی اور کم ہوگی۔ اس لئے غلام کی بیچ ہو گئی۔ یہی حال اپنے غلام اور دوسرے غلام کو ملانے کا ہے۔
اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ مبیع کے ساتھ دوسری بیع مال ہے اور بکنے کے قابل ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں مبیع کی لیکن کسی وجہ سے دوسری طبیع نہ بک سکی تو پہلی مبیع بیع میں داخل ہوگی۔ اور اس کی قیمت اس کے حصے کے مطابق لازم ہوگی ۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت جابر فرماتے ہیں کہ آپ نے مد بر غلام کو بیچا ہے۔
[902](21) If someone combines a slave and a mudabbir, or his own slave and another's slave in a sale, then the sale is valid only for the (regular) slave with its share of the price.
If he combined a regular slave and a mudabbir in one sale, or his own slave and another's slave without his permission in one sale, then the sale of the mudabbir will not occur, but the sale of the pure (regular) slave will occur. And the price that corresponds to its share will be obligatory. For example, if the slave and mudabbir were worth two thousand, and the pure slave's price is one thousand, then one thousand is obligatory. Similarly, another's slave without his permission will not be included in the sale, but one's own slave's sale will occur, and the price of its share will be obligatory on the buyer. The mudabbir, according to some imams, is salable like a slave, so it is property. There is a hadith: from Jabir, he said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) sold a mudabbir. (Bukhari, Book of Sales of Mudabbir, p. 297, no. 223). From this hadith, it is known that a mudabbir is salable. So when he combined it with a pure slave, the sale took place. Now, due to the non-sale of the mudabbir later, its price will be separate and reduced, so the slave's sale occurred. The same applies to combining one's own slave with another's slave.
The principle: This issue is based on the principle that the second sold item (accompanying the first) is property and salable. So both are sold, but if the second cannot be sold for some reason, then the first (valid) sold item remains in the sale, and its price is due according to its share.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the validity of a sale that combines a regular slave with a mudabbir (a slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death) or with another person's slave. The Hanafi ruling is that the sale of the regular slave is valid, but the sale of the mudabbir or the other's slave is not executed. The buyer pays only the proportionate price of the regular slave. The mudabbir is considered property because the Prophet (peace be upon him) sold a mudabbir (as reported by Jabir in Bukhari), so it is a valid subject of sale. However, if the mudabbir is combined with a regular slave in one contract, the mudabbir's sale is not valid (in this context, because of a legal impediment perhaps related to the promise of freedom), but since it is salable in itself, the contract is not entirely void; rather, the regular slave's sale is valid. If the mudabbir's sale is not possible (e.g., due to the master's death), the buyer pays only the price of the regular slave. The same principle applies if one sells his own slave together with another's slave without the other's permission: the other's slave is not included, but the sale of one's own slave is valid. The author states the principle: if two items are sold together, both being property and salable, but one cannot be sold due to a reason, the sale of the valid item remains effective with its share of the price. This is a typical Hanafi application of the concept of partial validity in sales.

Key Terms
المدبر (al-mudabbir): A slave whom the master has promised freedom after his death; he is considered property but with a right of future emancipation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person sells his own slave together with another person's slave without that person's permission, what is the ruling on the sale of his own slave?
A) The sale of his own slave is invalid.
B) The sale of his own slave is valid and the buyer pays its share of the price.
C) The entire contract is void.
D) The sale of his own slave depends on the other owner's consent.

Key Takeaway
When two items are sold together and one cannot be sold, the sale of the valid item remains effective with its share of the price.
